Talaq — Divorce
beginner
8 min
The Three Types of Divorce: Ahsan, Hasan, and Bid'i
Classification of divorce into three types with definitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define and distinguish the three types of divorce (ahsan, hasan, bid'i) and explain the legal meaning of 'sunnah' and 'bid'i' in the context of divorce according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Divorce is mubah but detested; 'sunnah' divorce incurs no blame, while 'bid'i' incurs blame—both are effective.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah opens the Book of Divorce by classifying divorce into three categories. Understanding these categories is essential because the ruling of divorce changes based on how it is performed. The commentator clarifies that 'sunnah' divorce does not imply reward but merely absence of blame, and 'bid'i' divorce is not the same as generic innovation—it specifically refers to a divorce that incurs legal censure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
Find the three types listed: ahsan (best), hasan (good), and bid'i (innovative). Note that masnun (sunnah) covers the first two.
Ahsan is one revocable divorce in a pure state; hasan is three divorces in three pure periods.
2
Understand 'masnun' in this context
The text says masnun does NOT mean reward-worthy, but rather 'free from blame.' Divorce is not worship, so reward is not earned for the act itself—only for avoiding sin.
This is a key Hanafi nuance: 'sunnah' here equals mubah (permissible) without blame.
3
Distinguish bid'i from general innovation
Bid'i divorce does not refer to the well-known concept of religious innovation; it specifically means a divorce that incurs legal blame (عتاب شرعي). Examples: divorcing during menstruation, after intercourse, or triple divorce in one sentence.
Bid'i divorce is haram but legally effective.
4
Grasp the basic ruling of divorce
The text states divorce is 'the most detested of permissible things' (أبغض المباحات). Its basic ruling is mubah, but it may become wajib, mustahabb, makruh, or haram depending on circumstances.
This is the foundation for all further rulings on divorce.

The best of them. The Book of Divorce. Know that they divided divorce into three categories: ahsan (best), hasan (good), and bid'i (innovative). The sunnah (recommended) includes the first two. Bid'i is derived from bid'a (innovation) and is opposite to sunnah. The meaning of sunnah here is that which is established in a way that does not incur blame, not that it brings reward, for divorce is not an act of worship in itself to obtain reward; what is meant here is permissible (mubah). Yes, if he has an inclination to divorce her in a bid'i manner and restrains himself to the sunnah, he is rewarded for restraining himself from sin, not for the divorce itself, for it is the most detested of permissible things. Thus it becomes clear that bid'i in the context of divorce does not mean its well-known meaning (i.e., something not present in the first three generations and not supported by a legal proof), but rather what incurs legal blame upon its occurrence. If you say: How can divorce be hasan or ahsan while it is the most detested of permissible things? (Then the response is given in the footnote...)
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage begins the Book of Divorce in the commentary. It classifies divorce into three types: Ahsan (best), Hasan (good), and Bid'i (innovative). The term 'sunnah' divorce encompasses the first two types. Bid'i divorce is contrasted with sunnah; it is called 'bid'i' because it involves an innovation contrary to the sunnah. The commentator clarifies that 'sunnah' here does not mean an act that yields reward, because divorce is not an act of worship; rather it means an act that does not incur blame. The underlying ruling is that divorce is mubah (permissible) but it is the most detested of permissible things (أبغض المباحات). However, if a person refrains from a bid'i divorce and opts for a sunnah one, he is rewarded for avoiding sin, not for the divorce itself. The term 'bid'i' in the context of divorce is not the same as the general concept of innovation (bid'a) condemned in religion; rather it specifically refers to a divorce that, if performed, incurs legal blame (عتاب شرعي). The commentator then anticipates a question: how can divorce be hasan or ahsan if it is the most detested of permissible things? The answer (in the footnote) elaborates that divorce can take various rulings depending on circumstances: it can be mubah (when there is need due to incompatibility), mustahabb (if the wife is abusive), makruh (ba'in divorce in the apparent narration), wajib (if the husband cannot fulfill marital duties due to impotence), and haram (divorce during menstruation or in a pure state where intercourse occurred, or triple divorce in one statement). This classification clarifies that the same act can have different legal rulings based on context.

Key Terms
طلاق أحسن (ṭalāq aḥsan): The best divorce: one pronouncement in a non-menstrual period without intercourse, followed by waiting period without revoking.
طلاق حسن (ṭalāq ḥasan): Good divorce: three pronouncements in three successive pure states, each followed by no intercourse.
طلاق بدعي (ṭalāq bidʿī): Innovative divorce: divorce that incurs legal blame, such as divorcing during menstruation or in a pure state after intercourse, or triple divorce in one sentence.
مسنون (masnūn): Recommended divorce, which includes both aḥsan and ḥasan. Does not necessarily mean rewarding, but rather free from blame.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the meaning of 'masnun' divorce?
A) A divorce that brings reward because it follows the sunnah.
B) A divorce that is established in a way that does not incur blame and is considered permissible.
C) A divorce that is recommended and mustahabb.
D) A divorce that is performed exactly as the Prophet did.

Key Takeaway
Divorce is classified into ahsan, hasan, and bid'i; the 'sunnah' types are blame-free, while bid'i is sinful but effective, and the basic ruling is mubah but detested.

The Ahsan Talaq: Conditions for the Best Mode of Divorce
Defines three types of talaq and details conditions of ahsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the four conditions of ahsan talaq and distinguish it from hasan and bid'i talaq.

Core Idea
Ahsan talaq: one revocable pronouncement in a tuhr without intercourse — the least blameworthy mode.

Divorce (talaq) is the most detested permissible act, yet its modes differ in blameworthiness. The Hanafi school classifies talaq into three types: ahsan (best), hasan (good), and bid'i (innovatory). This lesson unpacks the ahsan talaq — the preferred mode — and its four essential conditions as explained in the commentary. Understanding these conditions helps a Muslim avoid blameworthy divorces and follow the sunna.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types
From the passage, state the three divisions of talaq: ahsan, hasan, and bid'i. Note that 'masnun' covers the first two.
Bid'i here means 'blameworthy,' not the usual 'innovation in religion.'
2
Extract the conditions of ahsan
Read the passage carefully and list the four conditions for a talaq to be ahsan: one pronouncement, revocable (raj'i), in a tuhr, and that tuhr free from intercourse.
The passage explicitly states these conditions; note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on ba'in as bid'i.
3
Understand the rationale
Explain why each condition matters—e.g., one pronouncement avoids multiplicity, revocability allows reconciliation, tuhr without intercourse ensures clarity of 'idda.
The author notes that if the woman is pregnant or non-menstruating, the 'no intercourse' condition may be waived.
4
Distinguish hasan and bid'i
Hasan is three divorces in separate tuhrs; bid'i includes divorce during menstruation, in a tuhr with intercourse, or three divorces in one utterance.
Also note: a single ba'in divorce is bid'i in the apparent narrations.

[٢] قوله : في طهر ; - بالضم - هو مدة ما بين الحيضين أو زمان عدم رؤية الدم، وفي إطلاقه إشارة إلى أنه يستوي فيه أوله وآخره ، قيل : الثاني أولى ; احتراز عن تطويل العدّة ، وقيل : الأول أولى. كذا في «النهر»(۳).
(۱) يعني أن أحسن الطرق تطليقها طلقة واحدة في طهر لا وطء فيه وتركها حتى تنقضي عدتها. ينظر: «درر الحكام (۱ : ٢٥٩). (۲) «النهر الفائق (۲ : ۳۱۱). (۳) (النهر الفائق (۲ : ۳۱۱).
The best. Book of Divorce. [1] His statement: 'The best...' etc.; know that they divided divorce into three divisions: best (ahsan), good (hasan), and innovatory (bid'i). And the sunnah-approved (al-masnun) encompasses the first two. And al-bid'i - with kasra of the bā' (it is) attributed to innovation (bid'a), and it is opposite to sunnah. And the meaning of al-masnun here is what is established in a way that does not incur blame, not that it merits reward; for divorce is not an act of worship in itself such that reward is attained through it. So what is meant here is the permissible (mubah). Yes, if he has an inclination to divorce her in a bid'i way but restrains himself to the sunni way, he is rewarded for restraining himself from disobedience, not for the divorce itself, for it is the most detested of permissible things. This is verified in 'al-Fath' and others. And by this it becomes clear that al-bid'i in the discussion of divorce is not meant in its well-known meaning, i.e., what does not exist in the three generations and is not supported by a legal evidence, as is said regarding other actions, 'this is an innovation and this is innovatory.' Rather, what is meant is what incurs legal blame by its occurrence. If you say: How can divorce be good or best while it is the most detested of permissible things? (Footnote 1 about five rulings of divorce). [2] Only one divorce in a tuhr (pure period) in which there was no intercourse. I say: It is... and in itself, although it is the most detested of permissible things, the ways of its occurrence vary in number and time, so divorce acquires these descriptions by virtue of them, not by virtue of its essence. Then the best (ahsan) is superior to the good (hasan); therefore the name of preference is applied to it. [1] His statement: 'divorce' (talqa) - with fatha on tā', lām, and tā' marbūṭa, and what is meant is revocable (raj'iyyah). The gist is that the best divorce (al-ahsan) is only realized when multiple attributes exist in number and time. First: that it be one. If it is more than one, then if it is with one word and in one time, it is bid'i; if it is separate, it is hasan. And his statement 'only' indicates that no other divorce follows it, even in another tuhr. Ibn Abi Shayba narrated from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i that he said: 'They used to recommend that he divorces her once, then leaves her until she menstruates three times.' Second: that it be revocable. As for the single irrevocable (ba'in) divorce, it is bid'i in the apparent narrations, and in the narration of al-Ziyadat: it is not disliked. This is in al-Fath. Third: that it be in a tuhr. Fourth: that this tuhr be one in which no intercourse has occurred. So divorce during menstruation is bid'i, and similarly in a tuhr in which he had intercourse, and similarly in a tuhr where intercourse occurred in the preceding menstruation. And if he divorces in a tuhr without intercourse after the appearance of pregnancy, or she is one who does not menstruate, in a tuhr in which he had intercourse with her, it is not bid'i due to the absence of the cause, i.e., relying on the 'idda. This is in al-Nahr. And by this it is clear that in explaining the best (ahsan) additional conditions are also necessary. [2] His statement: 'in a tuhr' - with damm - it is the period between two menstruations or the time of not seeing blood. And in its absolute mention there is indication that its beginning and end are equal. It is said: the second is better, to avoid prolonging the 'idda; and it is said: the first is better. This is in al-Nahr. (Footnotes about references).
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah is a commentary explaining the classification of talaq (divorce) into three types: ahsan, hasan, and bid'i. The author first clarifies that 'masnun' (sunna-approved) covers both ahsan and hasan. Bid'i here does not mean the usual 'innovation' but rather any divorce that incurs legal blame. The famous hadith that divorce is 'the most detested of permissible things' (abghad al-mubahat) raises the question: how can it be called 'ahsan' or 'hasan'? The answer is that while divorce itself is detestable, its modes differ; the description is based on the manner of divorce (number, timing), not its essence. The ahsan divorce is a single revocable pronouncement in a tuhr (pure period) in which no intercourse occurred. The passage then details the four conditions: (1) only one divorce, not more; (2) it must be raj'i (revocable), as a single ba'in divorce is considered bid'i in the apparent narrations (though a narration from al-Ziyadat does not dislike it); (3) it must occur in a tuhr; (4) that tuhr must be free from intercourse. Additional nuances are given: if pregnancy is apparent or if the woman is non-menstruating, the condition of no intercourse may be waived. The passage concludes with a discussion on the definition of tuhr and a minor issue whether the beginning or end of tuhr is better for pronouncing divorce. Throughout, the commentary sources works like al-Fath and al-Nahr al-Fa'iq.

Key Terms
أحسن (ahsan): The best form of divorce: one revocable pronouncement in a pure period (tuhr) without intercourse.
بدعي (bid'i): A divorce that incurs legal blame, such as during menstruation or in a tuhr with intercourse.
رجعية (raj'iyyah): Revocable divorce — the husband may take her back during the 'idda without a new marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum number of conditions for a divorce to be considered 'ahsan'?
A) One condition: it must be one pronouncement.
B) Four conditions: one pronouncement, revocable, in a tuhr, and no intercourse in that tuhr.
C) Two conditions: in a tuhr and no intercourse.
D) Three conditions: one pronouncement, revocable, and in a tuhr.

Key Takeaway
A divorce is ahsan only when it is a single revocable pronouncement in a tuhr without intercourse.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
6 min
Conditions of the Best (Ahsan) Divorce
Defines the four conditions of the best divorce (ahsan).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four conditions of the aḥsan divorce according to the Hanafi school and explain why violating each condition makes the divorce bid‘ī.

Core Idea
The best divorce is a single revocable pronouncement in a pure period without intercourse — any deviation makes it less than ideal.

Marriage dissolution in Islam follows a graded spectrum. The most meritorious form, the aḥsan divorce, requires precise conditions regarding the number, revocability, timing, and absence of intercourse. In this passage from the commentary on al-Wiqāyah, the scholar unpacks these four conditions. Understanding them is essential for any Muslim seeking to follow the Prophetic guidance on divorce.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is divorce (talāq). The ruling for the aḥsan form is sunnah muakkadah (emphasized recommendation). The text defines the conditions to achieve this superior form.
2
List the four conditions from the text
The commentator explicitly states four conditions: (1) single pronouncement, (2) revocable (rajʿī), (3) occurs in a period of purity (ṭuhr), (4) that ṭuhr has no intercourse. Write them down with the Arabic terms.
The matn says: 'ṭalqah faqaṭ fī ṭuhr lā waṭ'a fīh'
3
Examine the proof
The author cites the practice of the early Muslims (from Ibrāhīm al-Nakhaʿī) who preferred a single divorce followed by waiting for three menstrual cycles. This shows the basis for the first and timing conditions.
The proof is the practice of the salaf, not a direct Qur'an or hadith citation.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute on revocability
The passage mentions that a single irrevocable divorce (bāʾin) is considered bidʿī in the manifest narrations (Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah), but in the narration of al-Ziyādāt it is not disliked. Know the muftā bihī: the manifest position is that it is bidʿī.
This dispute affects whether a single irrevocable divorce can be considered aḥsan.
5
Identify exceptions
The text provides exceptions: if pregnancy is apparent or the woman is non-menstruating (e.g., post-menopausal or young), the ruling changes because the purpose of the waiting period is already achieved. In such cases, divorce is not bidʿī even if intercourse occurred.
The cause (ʿillah) is the reliance on the ʿiddah (waiting period).

طلقة فقط في طهر لا وطء فيه. قوله : طلقة ؛ بفتح الطاء واللام والتاء فيه الموحدة، والمراد به الرجعية، والحاصل أن الطلاق الأحسن إنما يوجد إذا وجدت أوصاف عديدة عدداً وزماناً. الأول : أن يكون واحداً ، فإن كان زائداً عليه فإن كان بكلمة واحدة وفي زمان واحد فهو بدعي، وإن كان متفرقاً ، فهو حسن وأشار بقوله : «فقط» إلى أن لا يوجد بعده طلاق آخر، ولو في طهر آخر، فقد أخرج ابن أبي شيبة عن إبراهيم النخعي له قال : «كانوا يستحبون أن يُطلقها واحدة ثم يتركها حتى تحيض ثلاث حيض. والثاني : أن يكون رجعياً، وأما الواحدة البائنة، فهي بدعية في ظاهر الروايات ، وفي رواية «الزيادات»: لا تكره. كذا في «الفتح». والثالث : أن يكون في طهر. والرابع : أن يكون ذلك الطهر لم يقع فيه وطء، فالطلاق في حالة الحيض بدعي، وكذا في طهر وطئ فيه وكذا في طهر وقع الوطء في حيض قبله، ولو طلق في طهر لا وطء فيه بعد ظهور الحبل أو كانت ممن لا تحيض في طهر وطئها فيه لا يكون بدعيّاً ؛ لعدم العلة؛ أي تعويل العدة عليها. كذا في «النهر»، وبهذا ظهر أنه لا بد في بيان الأحسن من قيود أخر أيضاً. قوله : في طهر ؛ - بالضم - هو مدة ما بين الحيضين أو زمان عدم رؤية الدم، وفي إطلاقه إشارة إلى أنه يستوي فيه أوله وآخره ، قيل : الثاني أولى ؛ احتراز عن تطويل العدّة ، وقيل : الأول أولى. كذا في «النهر».
A single divorce in a period of purity without intercourse. His saying: 'ṭalqah' (a divorce) with fatḥa on ṭā, lām, and tā with tā marbūṭa, and what is intended is the revocable (rajʿī) divorce. The summary is that the best divorce (al-aḥsan) only exists if several conditions are met: first, that it is one; if more than one, if it is with one word and in one time it is innovated (bidʿī), and if it is separated, it is good (ḥasan). And he indicated by his saying 'only' that no other divorce should occur after it, even in another period of purity. Ibn Abī Shaybah narrated from Ibrāhīm al-Nakhaʿī that he said: 'They used to prefer that he divorces her once, then leaves her until she experiences three menstrual cycles.' Second, that it be revocable; as for the single irrevocable divorce, it is innovated in the manifest narrations, and in the narration of al-Ziyādāt: it is not disliked. Thus in al-Fatḥ. Third, that it be in a period of purity. Fourth, that that period of purity be one in which no intercourse occurred. Divorce during menstruation is innovated, likewise in a period of purity in which intercourse occurred, and likewise in a period of purity where intercourse occurred in the previous menstruation. If he divorces in a period of purity without intercourse after the appearance of pregnancy, or if she is one who does not menstruate, then it is not innovated due to absence of the cause; that is, the reliance on the waiting period. Thus in al-Nahr. And by this it becomes clear that additional restrictions are necessary to explain the best. His saying: 'fī ṭuhr' (in a period of purity) – with ḍamma – it is the period between two menstruations or the time of not seeing blood. In its absolute expression is an indication that its beginning and end are equal. It was said: the second is better as a precaution against prolonging the waiting period, and it was said: the first is better. Thus in al-Nahr.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharḥ) on the definition of the best divorce (al-ṭalāq al-aḥsan) from the matn 'Ṭalqah faqaṭ fī ṭuhr lā waṭ'a fīh.' The commentator explains that the best divorce requires four conditions: (1) it must be a single pronouncement; (2) it must be revocable (rajʿī); (3) it must occur in a period of purity (ṭuhr); and (4) that period of purity must be free of intercourse. If any of these conditions is violated, the divorce becomes innovated (bidʿī) or at least not the best. The commentator cites narrations from Ibrāhīm al-Nakhaʿī showing the preference for a single divorce followed by waiting for three menstrual cycles. The revocability condition: a single irrevocable divorce (bāʾin) is considered bidʿī in the manifest narrations, but in one narration from al-Ziyādāt it is not disliked. The purity condition: divorce during menstruation or in a period of purity where intercourse occurred is bidʿī. Exception: if pregnancy is apparent or the woman is non-menstruating, divorce is not bidʿī even if intercourse had occurred, because the purpose of the waiting period (observing purity for ʿiddah) is already achieved. The discussion also addresses whether the beginning or end of the period of purity is preferred, with two opinions mentioned.

Key Terms
طلاق أحسن (ṭalāq aḥsan): The best form of divorce: a single revocable pronouncement in a period of purity without intercourse.
بدعي (bidʿī): Innovated divorce, disapproved (makruh tahrimi), such as triple pronouncement in one sitting or divorce during menstruation.
رجعية (rajʿiyyah): Revocable divorce; the husband can take his wife back without a new contract during the waiting period.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT a condition for the best (ahsan) divorce?
A) The divorce is a single pronouncement.
B) The divorce is irrevocable (bāʾin).
C) The divorce occurs in a period of purity (ṭuhr).
D) The period of purity is free of intercourse.

Key Takeaway
The aḥsan divorce requires four conditions: single pronouncement, revocability, purity, and no intercourse; violating any condition makes it bid‘ī.

The Good (Hasan) Divorce: Definition, Conditions, and Proof
Defines the good divorce and its conditions with proof from hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of the good divorce (hasan/sunni), distinguish it from the best divorce (ahsan), and apply the conditions for consummated and non-consummated wives.

Core Idea
The good divorce (hasan) is a single pronouncement for a non-consummated wife, valid even during menstruation.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah defines the good divorce (hasan) and clarifies why it is specifically called 'sunni'. The author addresses an objection that the best divorce (ahsan) should also be called sunni, providing two answers: refuting Imam Malik's restrictive view, and explaining Hanafi conventional usage. The passage then details the two sunnah aspects of divorce—number and time—and distinguishes between consummated and non-consummated wives. The proof is the well-known hadith of Ibn Umar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition
The matn states: 'And its good (hasan) which is the sunni: a single divorce for the non-consummated wife, even during menstruation.' Identify the key elements: one pronouncement, non-consummated, any time.
Note the term 'sunni' is used exclusively for the hasan divorce in Hanafi terminology.
2
Understand the objection
The commentator raises an objection: if the good is sunni, why is the best not also called sunni? The apparent meaning of the matn seems to exclude the best. Recognize that both are from the Sunnah.
The objection arises from a literal reading; the commentator resolves it.
3
Analyze the response
Two answers are given: (1) to refute Malik who held that exceeding one pronouncement is not sunni; the best is even more clearly sunni by primary inference. (2) In Hanafi usage, the term 'sunni' is conventionally applied to the good only, though both are sunnah.
The first answer is substantive; the second is terminological.
4
Distinguish conditions
Sunnah in divorce has two aspects: number (single pronouncement, applies to all) and time. For a consummated wife, the time must be a period of purity (tuhr) without intercourse. For a non-consummated wife, any time including menstruation is valid.
The difference is due to the purpose of iddah: for the consummated, purity ensures correct iddah calculation.
5
Examine the proof
The hadith of Ibn Umar: when he divorced his wife during her menses, the Prophet ordered him to take her back and then divorce her in a period of purity. This indicates that divorce during menses is not sunni for a consummated wife. For the non-consummated, the prohibition lifts because there is no iddah based on purity.
The hadith is narrated by al-Daraqutni and al-Nasa'i; its thubut and dalala are zanni.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحسنه وهو السني : طلقة لغير الموطوءة ولو في حيض قوله : وهو السني ؛ - بالضم - ، نسبة إلى السنة ، ويَرِدُ عليه : أنّ ظاهره يحكم بأن الأول ليس بسني مع أنه ليس كذلك ، فقد صرحوا بأن الأحسن والحسن كلاهما من أقسام المسنون ، مع أنّ الحَسَنَ لَمَّا كان سُنياً كان الأحسنُ سنياً بالطريق الأولى. وأجيب عنه : بأنه خصه بالذكر، ردّاً لقول مالك له، فإنّ عنده الزيادة على الواحد غير سنيّة، وحكم الأحسن يفهم بالطريق الأولى، أو يقال : إن السني وإن كان صادقاً على الحسن والأحسن كليهما، لكنّهم خصوا باسم السُّني الحسن ولم يطلقوا هذا في محاوراتهم على الأحسن، فلذلك خَصه بالذكر، فالمعنى وهـو السني في إطلاقاتهم، ووجه تخصيص إطلاقهم هو ما مر ر آنفاً. قوله : ولو في حيض ؛ الواو وصليّة ؛ أي ولو كان ذلك في حالة الحيض ، والحاصل أن السنّة في الطلاق من وجهين العدد والوقت فالعدد : هو أن لا يزيد على الواحد بكلمة واحدة، ولا فرق فيه بين المدخولة وغير المدخولة، لكنّه في المدخولة خاص بكونه في طهر خال عن الوطء، وفي غيرها لا فرق في كونه في طهر أو في حيض ؛ لأنَّ الوقت أعني الطهر الخالي عن الجماع خاص بالمدخولة. والأصل في هذا الباب قوله الله لابن عمر الله حين طلق امرأته في الحيض: «السنةُ أن تستقبل الطهر، وتطلق لكل قرء ، وأمره رسول الله الله بالمراجعة، وقال: إذا طهرت فطلق عند ذلك أو أمسك)، أخرجه الدارقطني. وعنه له أنه قال: «طلاق السنّة أن يطلّقها تطليقة وهي طاهرة من غير جماع ، فإذا حاضت وطهرت طلقها أخرى (۳) ، أخرجه النسائي، ومثله في الصحيحين وغيرهما.
And its good (hasan) which is the sunni: a single divorce for the non-consummated wife, even during menstruation. His saying: 'which is the sunni' – with ḍamma – attributed to the Sunnah. And it is objected: its apparent meaning judges that the first (i.e., ahsan) is not sunni, while it is not so; for they have stated that both the best and the good are from the divisions of the sunnah, and since the good is sunni, the best is sunni by primary inference. The answer: he mentioned it specifically to refute the saying of Malik, for according to him, exceeding one is not sunni; and the ruling of the best is understood by primary inference. Or it is said: although 'sunni' is true for both the good and the best, they have specified the name 'sunni' for the good and did not apply it in their usage to the best, therefore he specified it. So the meaning is: it is the sunni in their usage, and the reason for specification is as mentioned. His saying: 'even during menstruation'; the wāw is conjunctive; that is, even if that is in the state of menstruation. The summary is that the sunnah in divorce has two aspects: number and time. The number is that it should not exceed one with one word, and there is no difference between the consummated and non-consummated in this. However, for the consummated, it is specific to being in a period of purity free from intercourse. For other than her, there is no difference between being in a period of purity or in menstruation, because the time, i.e., the period of purity free from intercourse, is specific to the consummated wife. The basis for this chapter is the saying of Allah to Ibn ʿUmar when he divorced his wife during menstruation: 'The sunnah is that you should wait for the period of purity and divorce for each period of purity; and the Messenger of Allah ordered him to take her back and said: When she becomes pure, then divorce her at that time or keep her.' Narrated by al-Daraqutni. And from him (Ibn ʿUmar) that he said: 'The sunni divorce is that he divorces her once while she is pure without intercourse; then when she menstruates and becomes pure, he divorces her another time.' Narrated by al-Nasa'i, and similar in al-Sahihayn and others.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage defines the good divorce (al-ṭalāq al-ḥasan), also called sunnī. The matn states it is a single divorce for a non-consummated wife even during menstruation. The commentator addresses an objection: why is only the good called sunnī when the best (aḥsan) is also sunnī? The answer: first, to refute Imām Mālik who held that anything beyond one pronouncement is not sunnī; the best is even more clearly sunnī by primary inference. Second, in Hanafi usage, the term 'sunnī' is conventionally applied to the good, not the best, though both are from the sunnah. The passage then explains that sunnah in divorce has two aspects: number (single pronouncement) and time. For a consummated wife, the time must be a period of purity (ṭuhr) without intercourse; for a non-consummated wife, divorce is valid even during menstruation. The proof is the well-known hadith of Ibn ʿUmar (may Allah be pleased with him) when he divorced his wife during her menses. The Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered him to take her back and then divorce her in a period of purity. The hadith indicates that divorce during menstruation is forbidden (for the consummated wife) but for the non-consummated wife, the prohibition does not apply since there is no need to observe purity for ʿiddah. The commentator also cites another narration explaining the sunni divorce as a single pronouncement in purity.

Key Terms
طلاق سني (ṭalāq sunnī): The good divorce (hasan): a single pronouncement for a non-consummated wife, valid even during menstruation.
موطوءة (mawṭūʾah): A wife who has been consummated (i.e., intercourse has occurred).
قرء (qar'): Period of purity between menses; also interpreted as menstruation itself according to different schools.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because the best divorce involves more than one pronouncement.
D) Because Imām Malik argued that anything beyond one is not Sunnah.

Key Takeaway
The good divorce (hasan) is a single pronouncement for a non-consummated wife, valid even during menstruation; the term 'sunni' is conventionally applied only to it, though the best divorce is also from the Sunnah.

Sunni Talaq: Conditions and Types
Defining hasan (sunni) divorce and its conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions of sunni (hasan) divorce and distinguish its application to intercourse and non-intercourse women.

Core Idea
Sunni divorce is one utterance in a pure period for intercourse women; for others, any time, even menstruation.

The Hanafi school distinguishes between hasan (good) and ahsan (best) divorce, but restricts the term 'sunni' to hasan. This passage defines the conditions and proofs, clarifying that sunni divorce requires both correct number and timing, with special rules for non-intercourse women.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection about 'sunni' term
The commentator notes an apparent contradiction: if only hasan is called sunni, then ahsan would not be sunni. The answer explains that they restrict the term to hasan in refutation of Imam Malik, but ahsan is also sunni by primary inference.
This is a semantic specification for polemical context.
2
Identify the two aspects of sunni divorce
The sunnah in divorce has two aspects: number (one utterance) and time (purity period for intercourse women, any time for others). Number applies uniformly; time varies by type of woman.
For non-intercourse women, time is unrestricted even during menstruation.
3
Apply conditions to different women
For a woman with whom intercourse occurred: divorce must be in a pure period (tuhr) without intercourse. For a non-intercourse woman: no restriction; divorce is sunni even in menstruation.
The reasoning is that the waiting period (iddah) is known by menstruation or pregnancy; in non-intercourse women, there is no uncertainty.
4
Examine the evidence (dalil)
The basis is the hadith of Ibn Umar: the Prophet commanded him to take back his wife and divorce only in purity. Also reports from al-Daraqutni and al-Nasa'i specify: 'divorce her once while she is pure without intercourse.'
The hadith is ahad but accepted as proof for sunnah.
5
Note exception for non-menstruating women
For pregnant, minor (pre-menstrual), and post-menopausal women, months replace pure periods. They can be divorced in any state, even immediately after intercourse.
The reason for disapproval (ambiguity of iddah) is absent.

And its good (hasan) is the sunni: one divorce for the non-vagina-intercourse woman even if in menstruation. His statement: 'And it is the sunni' - with dammah - attributed to the Sunnah. An objection arises: its apparent meaning rules that the first (ahsan) is not sunni while it is not so, for they explicitly stated that both ahsan and hasan are types of sunnah; rather, when hasan is sunni, then ahsan is sunni by primary inference. And it was answered: that he specified it in mention, as a refutation of Malik's statement, for according to him the increase beyond one is not sunni, and the ruling of ahsan is understood by primary inference. Or it is said: The term sunni applies to both hasan and ahsan, but they restricted the name sunni to hasan and did not apply it in their discussions to ahsan; therefore he specified it in mention. So the meaning is: and it is the sunni in their usage, and the reason for their specification is as mentioned earlier. His statement: 'even if in menstruation' - the waw is conjunctive, meaning even if that occurs in a state of menstruation. The conclusion is that the sunnah in divorce is in two aspects: number and time. Number: that he not exceed one utterance with a single word, and there is no difference in that between the vagina-intercourse and non-vagina-intercourse woman. However, for the vagina-intercourse woman it is specific to being in a pure period free from intercourse, while for other than her there is no difference whether in purity or menstruation, because the time meaning the pure period free from intercourse is specific to the vagina-intercourse woman. The basis of this chapter is the statement of Allah to Ibn Umar when he divorced his wife in menstruation: 'The sunnah is that you await purity and divorce after each purity, and the Messenger of Allah commanded him to take her back and said: When she becomes pure, then divorce at that time or keep her.' Reported by al-Daraqutni. And from him that he said: 'The sunni divorce is that he divorces her once while she is pure without intercourse; then when she menstruates and becomes pure, he may divorce her another time.' Reported by al-Nasa'i, and similar in the two Sahihs and others. And for the vagina-intercourse woman, separation of the three in pure periods without intercourse in one who menstruates, and months for the post-menopausal, the minor girl, and the pregnant woman; according to the sunnah, three in three months, and it is permissible to divorce them immediately after intercourse. His statement: 'separation of three' meaning: effecting three divorces separately over three pure periods, each divorce in a purity without intercourse and preceded by menstruation. This is if she is menstruating; if she is not menstruating - being pregnant, a minor who does not menstruate, or reaching the age of menopause where menstruation has ceased - then months stand in place of pure periods as in the waiting period, and he divorces her each month one divorce. His statement: 'and it is permissible' means permissibility without dislike; meaning if he divorces the post-menopausal, minor, or pregnant woman in a purity in which he had intercourse, that is allowed, because the disapproval of divorce in a purity in which he had intercourse for menstruating women is only due to the possibility of pregnancy, where the basis of the waiting period (whether by menstruation or by giving birth) becomes ambiguous. This is absent in them due to the existence of pregnancy or its impossibility.

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn that defines the hasan (sunni) type of divorce. The author first clarifies that the term 'sunni' is used specifically for the hasan divorce (one utterance) to refute Imam Malik, who considers only one divorce as sunnah. Although the ahsan (best) divorce is also sunni, the commentators restrict the term 'sunni' to hasan in their usage. The conditions of sunni divorce involve both number (one utterance) and timing: for a women who has had intercourse, it must be in a pure period (tuhr) without intercourse; for a non-intercourse woman, there is no restriction, even during menstruation. The evidence cited is the hadith of Ibn Umar and other narrations from the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanding to divorce in purity. For women who do not menstruate (pregnant, minor, post-menopausal), months replace the pure periods, and it is permissible to divorce them immediately after intercourse because the reason for disapproval (ambiguity of waiting period) is absent.

Key Terms
السني (al-sunnī): Divorce that conforms to the Sunnah: a single divorce at the proper time (purity without intercourse for intercourse women, anytime for others).
الطلاق الحسن (al-ṭalāq al-ḥasan): The 'good' divorce: a single divorce at the appropriate time, constituting the sunni form.
غير الموطوءة (ghayr al-mawṭūʾah): A woman with whom intercourse has not occurred; she can be divorced even in menstruation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the maximum number of divorces allowed in a single utterance for a sunni divorce according to the Hanafi school?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) As many as the husband wishes

Key Takeaway
Sunni divorce requires exactly one utterance, with timing dependent on whether the woman has had intercourse: purity for intercourse women, any time for others.

Sunna Divorce: Conditions for Menstruating and Non-Menstruating Women
Defining sunna divorce with conditions for menstruating and non-menstruating women

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the requirements for sunna divorce for menstruating and non-menstruating women and identify the conditions for each.

Core Idea
Sunna divorce requires three separate divorces in three tuhrs without intercourse for menstruating women; for others, months replace tuhrs.

This lesson defines the sunna (recommended) method of divorce according to the Hanafi school. It distinguishes between women who menstruate and those who do not, specifying the intervals and prohibitions necessary for a valid sunna divorce. Understanding these conditions is essential for correctly applying the Prophet's guidance on divorce.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its category
Recognize that the passage defines 'sunna divorce' (al-ṭalāq al-sunnī), which is the recommended form. For a menstruating woman, it requires three separate divorces in three distinct periods of purity (tuhr), each without intercourse.
Sunna divorce is contrasted with bid'a divorce, which violates these conditions.
2
List conditions for menstruating women
Extract the three conditions: (1) Three separate tuhrs, (2) No intercourse in each tuhr, (3) Each tuhr preceded by a menstruation.
The divorce must be pronounced in the tuhr, not in menstruation.
3
Identify conditions for non-menstruating women
For pregnant, minor, and menopausal women, months (shuhūr) replace tuhrs. The husband gives one divorce per month for three months.
The 'idda for such women is also three months, so this aligns.
4
Understand the 'illa for permissibility after intercourse
The passage explains that for menstruating women, divorce in a tuhr with intercourse is disliked due to possible pregnancy causing ambiguity in the 'idda. For non-menstruating women, this ambiguity is absent, so such divorce is permissible without dislike.
The ruling is based on the underlying reason (ʿilla), not just the form.
5
Distinguish from bid'a divorce
Note that violating these conditions (e.g., three divorces at once or during menstruation) results in a bid'a divorce, which is valid (the divorce falls) but sinful.
The Hanafi school holds that bid'a divorce is effective, unlike some other schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وللموطوءة تفريق الثلاث في أطهار لا وطء فيها فيمن تحيض ، وأشهر في الآيسة والصغيرة والحامل للسنة ثلاثاً في ثلاثة أشهر : فقوله : وأشهر عطف على أطهار، وحل طلاقهنَّ عقيب الوطء .

[1] قوله : تفريق الثلاث ؛ أي إيقاعُ ثلاث تطليقات متفرقة في أطهار ثلاثة كلّ طلاق في طهر لا وطء فيه، وفي حيض قبله ، وهذا إذا كانت حائضة، فإن لم تكن حائضة بأن كانت حاملة أو صغيرة لا تحيض، أو بالغة إلى سن الإياس قد انقطع عنها الحيض، فالأشهر في حقها قائمة مقام الأطهار كما في العدة، فيطلقها في كل شهر طلاقا.

[2] قوله : وحل ؛ المراد به الحلّ من غير كراهة ، يعني إن طلق الآيسة والصغيرة والحبلى في طهر وطئ فيه جاز ذلك ؛ لأنَّ كراهة الطلاق في طهرِ وَطِئَ فيه في ذواتِ الحيض إنما هي لتوهم الحبل، فيشتبه وجه العدّة أهو بالحيض أم بوضع الحمل، وهي مفقودة فيهن لوجود الحبل أو عدم احتماله.
And for the one who is sexually intercourse is permissible, the separation of three [divorces] in intervals of purity (tuhr) without intercourse in them for those who menstruate, and months for the post-menopausal, the minor, and the pregnant according to the sunna: three in three months. So his saying: 'and months' is co-ordinated with 'intervals of purity' [in grammatical connection]. And the permissibility of divorcing them immediately after intercourse.

[1] His saying: 'separation of the three' i.e., effecting three separate divorces in three intervals of purity, each divorce in an interval of purity without intercourse in it, and with menstruation before it. This is if she is menstruating. If she is not menstruating - such as being pregnant, or a minor who does not menstruate, or a woman who has reached the age of menopause and menstruation has ceased - then months take the place of intervals of purity, as in the waiting period ('idda). So he divorces her with one divorce in each month.

[2] His saying: 'and the permissibility' means permissibility without dislike. That is, if he divorces the post-menopausal, the minor, or the pregnant in an interval of purity in which he had intercourse, that is permissible, because the dislike of divorce in an interval of purity in which intercourse occurred for those who menstruate is only due to the possibility of pregnancy, so the mode of the waiting period becomes ambiguous - whether it is by menstruation or by delivery - and that [ambiguity] is absent in them due to the existence of pregnancy or the impossibility of it.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage defines the sunna (recommended) form of divorce. The commentator explains that for a woman who menstruates, the sunna method is to give three separate divorces, each in a different tuhr (interval between two menses) during which there has been no intercourse. The tuhr must be preceded by a menstruation. For women who do not menstruate (pregnant, minor, menopausal), months are substituted for tuhrs, as in the 'idda. The author then clarifies that it is permissible (without dislike) to divorce a pregnant, minor, or menopausal woman even if he has just had intercourse, because the reason for dislike in menstruating women (uncertainty about pregnancy) does not apply to them.

Key Terms
طهر (tuhr): The period of purity between two menstrual periods; in divorce rulings, it is the time in which a valid divorce can be given without intercourse.
بدعة (bid'a): An innovation; in divorce, it refers to a divorce that violates the sunna method, such as three divorces at once or divorce during menstruation.
آيسة (a'isah): A woman who has reached menopause and no longer menstruates.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Three tuhrs, each with one divorce

Key Takeaway
The sunna divorce method ensures clarity and avoids uncertainty by requiring separate intervals, differing for menstruating and non-menstruating women.

Bid'a Divorce and the General Dislike of Divorce
Defining bid'a divorce types and citing the hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the types of bid'a divorce, explain why it is sinful yet valid in the Hanafi school, and apply the hadith 'The most hateful of lawful things to Allah is divorce' to the legal status of divorce.

Core Idea
Bid'a divorce is valid but sinful — the act occurs, but the husband disobeys Allah by choosing a prohibited method.

Divorce is permissible but strongly discouraged. The Prophet ﷺ called it the most hateful of permissible things. When a husband divorces in a manner that violates the sunna (e.g., three divorces in one sitting or during menstruation), the divorce is still effective, but he commits a sin. Understanding bid'a divorce is crucial for distinguishing between the validity of the act and the moral culpability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of bid'a divorce
From the text, list the forms of bid'a divorce: three divorces with one word or separately in one tuhr, divorce during menstruation, and divorce in a tuhr where intercourse occurred.
The key is deviation from the sunna methods.
2
Understand the legal effect
Note that the Hanafi school rules such divorces as valid (the divorce occurs) but the husband sins (makruh tahrimi). This is the position of the majority of Companions and jurists.
Some early scholars held it invalid, but the majority view is relied upon.
3
Examine the nuance regarding revocation
If a husband divorces once, revokes (by word or kiss), then divorces again in the same tuhr, it is not disliked. But if revocation is by intercourse, then divorce is disliked because intercourse occurred in that tuhr.
This shows the importance of avoiding intercourse in a tuhr where divorce may follow.
4
Apply the hadith to the general ruling
The hadith 'أبغض الحلال إلى الله الطلاق' indicates divorce is permissible (halal) but extremely disliked. This underlies the Hanafi view that divorce is mubah but makruh tanzih, and bid'a forms are makruh tahrimi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : وبدعيه ثلاثاً ؛ أي مجتمعاً أو متفرّقاً، كأنت طالق ثلاثاً أو أنت طالق طالق طالق، فمثل هذا يقع ، لكنّه يأثم به هو المنقولُ عن جمهور الصحابة والتابعين والمجتهدين، منهم ابن عباس أخرجه عنه مالك ، وأبو هريرة له أخرجه عنه أبو داود.
وقال ابن الهمام في «فتح القدير»: «طلاقُ البدعة ما خالف كلا قسمي السنة ، وذلك بأن يطلقها ثلاثاً بكلمةٍ واحدةٍ أو متفرّقةٍ في طهر واحد أو اثنين كذلك، أو واحدة في الحيض، أو في طهر قد جامعها فيه، أو جامعها في الحيض الذي يليه، فإذا فعل ذلك وقع الطلاق، وكان عاصيا». انتهى

[3] قوله : في طهر لا رجعة فيه ؛ قيد لقرينه ؛ أي مرتين متفرقاً في طهر واحد لم يتخلل بين الطلقتين رجعة، فلو تخللت بأن طلق في طهر واحدة، ثم رجع : أي بالقول أو القبلة ونحوها، ثمّ طلّق ثانياً في ذلك الطهر لا يكره، نعم لو رجع بالوطء ثم طلق يكره ؛ لكونه في طهر وقع فيه وطء.
[4] قوله : وطئت ؛ أي ولم تكن حبلى ولا آيسة ولا صغيرة على ما مرّ.
[5] قوله : وتجب ؛ أي إذا طَلَّقَ حالة الحيض يجب أن يرجع بالوطء بعد انقضاء الحيض أو بالقول فيه ؛ رفعاً للمعصية بذلك أمر النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ابن عمر له حين طلق امرأته في الحيض، أخرجه البخاري، وغيره.
[6] قوله : أبغض المباحات ؛ الأصل فيه حديث : «أبغض الحلال إلى الله الطلاق» أخرجه أبو داود وابن ماجة والحاكم.
His saying: 'and his innovated [divorce] is three' i.e., together or separate, such as 'You are thrice divorced' or 'You are divorced, divorced, divorced.' Such [a divorce] occurs, but he sins by it. This is the transmitted view from the majority of the Companions, the Followers, and the independent jurists, among them Ibn 'Abbas (Malik narrated from him) and Abu Huraira (Abu Dawud narrated from him).
And Ibn al-Humam said in Fath al-Qadir: 'Bid'a divorce is what violates both types of sunna. That is, he divorces her three times with one word, or separately in one tuhr or two likewise, or one [divorce] during menstruation, or in a tuhr in which he had intercourse, or he had intercourse in the menstruation that follows it. If he does that, the divorce occurs, and he is disobedient.' End.

[3] His saying: 'in a tuhr without return' is a restriction for its counterpart; i.e., two [divorces] separately in one tuhr without revocation between the two divorces. If revocation intervenes - he divorces once in a tuhr, then revokes (by words or a kiss or the like), then divorces a second time in that same tuhr - it is not disliked. However, if he revokes by intercourse and then divorces, it is disliked, because it is in a tuhr in which intercourse occurred.
[4] His saying: 'and she is one with whom intercourse is permissible' i.e., she is not pregnant, menopausal, or a minor, as has passed.
[5] His saying: 'and it is obligatory' i.e., if he divorces during menstruation, he must revoke by intercourse after the menstruation ends or by words during it, to remove the disobedience. The Prophet commanded Ibn 'Umar to do so when he divorced his wife during menstruation; Bukhari and others narrated it.
[6] His saying: 'the most hateful of permissible things' - its basis is the hadith: 'The most hateful of lawful things to Allah is divorce' narrated by Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah, and al-Hakim.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This section defines bid'a (innovated) divorce. The commentator explains that bid'a divorce includes giving three divorces at once (whether in one phrase or separately in one sitting), giving two divorces in one tuhr without a revocation in between, divorcing during menstruation, or divorcing in a tuhr after intercourse. All such divorces are effective (the divorce occurs) but the husband sins. Then the commentator addresses a nuance: if a husband gives one divorce, then revokes (by word or action), then gives a second divorce in the same tuhr, it is not disliked (provided the revocation is not by intercourse). However, if he revokes by intercourse then divorces, it is disliked because of intercourse in that tuhr. The text also mentions the obligation of revocation if a husband divorces his wife during menstruation, based on the Prophet's command to Ibn 'Umar. Finally, the passage cites the famous hadith that divorce is the most hated permissible act, underlining its gravity.

Key Terms
بدعة (bid'a): Innovation; in divorce, any form that deviates from the sunna method.
أبغض المباحات (abghad al-mubahat): The most hateful of permissible things; a description of divorce.
رجعة (raj'a): Revocation of divorce during the 'iddah period, allowing the husband to take back his wife without a new marriage.
طهر (tuhr): The period of purity between menstruations, during which sunna divorce is allowed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Bid'a divorce is valid in effect but sinful in method; the husband must repent and, if possible, revoke to remove the disobedience.

Divorce in a Pure Period Without Revocability
States the ruling on divorcing twice in a single pure period without intervening return.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on two divorces in one pure period (tuhr) without intervening revocation, and identify when such a divorce is disliked.

Core Idea
Two divorces in one tuhr: halal unless revocation was by intercourse.

This lesson examines the precise conditions for valid divorce timing. The Hanafi school places great emphasis on the purity period (tuhr) as a necessary condition, but the presence or absence of revocation and the method of revocation affect the ruling on dislike.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The passage describes two divorces in a single tuhr without any revocation (raj'ah) between them. Alternatively, it considers a scenario where the first divorce was revoked, then a second divorce follows in the same tuhr.
If there is no revocation, the second divorce is valid and not disliked.
2
Determine if revocation intervened
If the husband revoked the first divorce by word or kiss (not intercourse), then divorced again in the same tuhr, the second divorce is valid and not disliked (la yukrah).
Revocation by word or kiss is permissible and does not corrupt the tuhr.
3
Check if revocation was by intercourse
If the husband revoked by intercourse, then divorced again in the same tuhr, the second divorce is disliked (yukrah) because the tuhr was 'contaminated' by intercourse.
Intercourse in a tuhr after a revocable divorce is allowed, but it makes a subsequent divorce in that tuhr disliked.
4
Conclude the ruling
The divorce is valid in all cases (sahih), but the level of dislike depends on the method of revocation. The ruling clarifies that the mere occurrence of two divorces in one tuhr is not problematic per se.
The dislikedness is makruh tanzih (slightly disliked) according to the text's wording.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق / أنواعه وشروطه

في طهر لا رجعة فيه أو واحدةٌ في طهرٍ لا وطئت فيه، أو حيض موطوءة وتجب رجعتها في الأصح، وعند بعض مشايخنا تستحب.

[1] قوله: في طهر لا رجعة فيه؛ قيد لقرينه؛ أي مرتين متفرقاً في طهر واحد لم يتخلل بين الطلقتين رجعة، فلو تخللت بأن طلق في طهر واحدة، ثم رجع: أي بالقول أو القبلة ونحوها، ثمّ طلّق ثانياً في ذلك الطهر لا يكره، نعم لو رجع بالوطء ثم طلق يكره؛ لكونه في طهر وقع فيه وطء.

[2] قوله: وطئت؛ أي ولم تكن حبلى ولا آيسة ولا صغيرة على ما مرّ.

[3] قوله: وتجب؛ أي إذا طَلَّقَ حالة الحيض يجب أن يرجع بالوطء بعد انقضاء الحيض أو بالقول فيه؛ رفعاً للمعصية بذلك أمر النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ابن عمر له حين طلق امرأته في الحيض، أخرجه البخاري وغيره.
The Book of Divorce / Its Types and Conditions. In a pure period without revocability, or one [divorce] in a pure period in which she was not sexually approached, or menstruation of one who was approached, and it is obligatory to return to her in the most correct view, and according to some of our mashayikh it is recommended. [1] His saying: 'in a pure period without revocability' is a restriction for the second [divorce]; i.e., two [divorces] separately in one pure period without a return intervening between the two divorces. If it intervened such that he divorced once in a pure period, then returned — by word or a kiss and the like — then divorced a second time in that pure period, it is not disliked. Yes, if he returned by intercourse then divorced, it is disliked because it is in a pure period in which intercourse occurred. [2] His saying: 'was approached' means she was not pregnant, not menopausal, and not a minor, as passed. [3] His saying: 'it is obligatory' means if he divorced during menstruation, he must return by intercourse after the end of menstruation or by word in it, to remove the sin. For this the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, ordered Ibn 'Umar when he divorced his wife during menstruation, narrated by al-Bukhari and others.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the matn of al-Wiqayah, expanded by the sharh. It addresses the conditions under which divorce is disliked or obligatory to revoke. The first part states that if a man divorces his wife twice in a single period of purity (tuhr) without having revoked the first divorce, or if he divorces her once in a tuhr where she was not approached, or if he divorces her during menstruation when she had been approached, then it is obligatory to revoke the divorce in the most correct position (al-asahh). Some Hanafi mashayikh consider it merely recommended (mustahab). The commentary clarifies: 'in a tuhr without revocability' applies to the second divorce — two divorces in one tuhr without intervening return. If the man divorces once, then returns by word or kiss, then divorces again in the same tuhr, it is not disliked. But if the return was by intercourse, then the second divorce is disliked because the tuhr was contaminated by intercourse. 'was approached' means the woman is not pregnant, menopausal, or a minor, as previously established. 'it is obligatory' refers to the case of divorcing during menstruation: the man must return to his wife after her menses ends, either by intercourse or by word, to lift the sin of divorcing in menstruation. This is based on the hadith where the Prophet ordered Ibn 'Umar to take back his wife when he divorced her during her period. The majority view (al-asahh) makes this return wajib, while some Hanafis hold it mustahab. The Hanafi school emphasizes that the command in the hadith indicates obligation unless evidence indicates recommendation.

Key Terms
طهر (tuhr): Period of purity between menstrual cycles, during which a woman is not menstruating.
رجعة (raj'ah): Revocation of a revocable divorce by word or action, returning the wife to marriage without a new contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The second divorce is invalid because the return was not by intercourse.
B) The second divorce is valid and not disliked.
C) The second divorce is valid but disliked because it occurred in the same tuhr.
D) The second divorce is valid but disliked because the return was by a kiss.

Key Takeaway
Two divorces in one pure period are valid and not disliked unless the first divorce was revoked by intercourse, in which case the second divorce becomes disliked (makruh tanzih).

Obligation to Revoke Divorce During Menstruation
States the obligation to revoke divorce during menstruation and the supporting hadith evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on revoking a divorce issued during menstruation, explain the dalil from the hadith of Ibn 'Umar, and identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on whether it is wajib or mustahab.

Core Idea
Divorce during menstruation is sinful; returning to her is wajib (al-asahh) to remove the sin.

This lesson focuses on the obligation to revoke (raj'ah) after issuing a divorce during menstruation. The Hanafi school relies on the explicit command of the Prophet to Ibn 'Umar, making the return wajib in the most correct view, though some early Hanafi scholars consider it only recommended. The ruling also specifies that the woman must have been 'approached' (non-pregnant, non-menopausal, non-minor) for the obligation to apply.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited act
Divorcing a wife during her menstruation is a sinful act (makruh tahrimi) because it violates the prophetic guidance to wait for a tuhr.
The divorce itself is valid but its timing is prohibited.
2
State the Hanafi ruling on revocation
After such a divorce, the husband must return to his wife (raj'ah) either by word or by intercourse after her menses ends. This is wajib according to al-asahh (the most correct view).
Some Hanafi mashayikh said it is mustahab (recommended).
3
Identify the dalil
The hadith of Ibn 'Umar: when he divorced his wife during menstruation, the Prophet ordered him to take her back.
The command 'amr' indicates obligation in Hanafi usul.
4
Analyze the usul principle
In Hanafi usul, the imperative (amr) from the Prophet, when it comes with a command to do an act, indicates wujub unless there is a qarinah (contextual clue) that changes it to recommendation. Here, no such qarinah is established, so the asahh is wujub.
The opponents rely on the fact that the command was given to a specific person (Ibn 'Umar) and may be specific.
5
Check the condition of the woman
The phrase 'موطوءة' (approached) means the woman must have been in a marital relationship where intercourse could have occurred; thus she is not pregnant, menopausal, or a minor. If she is one of these, the ruling may differ.
The condition ensures that the divorce is revocable and the waiting period applies.

كتاب الطلاق / أنواعه وشروطه

في طهر لا رجعة فيه أو واحدةٌ في طهرٍ لا وطئت فيه، أو حيض موطوءة وتجب رجعتها في الأصح، وعند بعض مشايخنا تستحب.

[1] قوله: في طهر لا رجعة فيه؛ قيد لقرينه؛ أي مرتين متفرقاً في طهر واحد لم يتخلل بين الطلقتين رجعة، فلو تخللت بأن طلق في طهر واحدة، ثم رجع: أي بالقول أو القبلة ونحوها، ثمّ طلّق ثانياً في ذلك الطهر لا يكره، نعم لو رجع بالوطء ثم طلق يكره؛ لكونه في طهر وقع فيه وطء.

[2] قوله: وطئت؛ أي ولم تكن حبلى ولا آيسة ولا صغيرة على ما مرّ.

[3] قوله: وتجب؛ أي إذا طَلَّقَ حالة الحيض يجب أن يرجع بالوطء بعد انقضاء الحيض أو بالقول فيه؛ رفعاً للمعصية بذلك أمر النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ابن عمر له حين طلق امرأته في الحيض، أخرجه البخاري وغيره.
The Book of Divorce / Its Types and Conditions. In a pure period without revocability, or one [divorce] in a pure period in which she was not sexually approached, or menstruation of one who was approached, and it is obligatory to return to her in the most correct view, and according to some of our mashayikh it is recommended. [1] His saying: 'in a pure period without revocability' is a restriction for the second [divorce]; i.e., two [divorces] separately in one pure period without a return intervening between the two divorces. If it intervened such that he divorced once in a pure period, then returned — by word or a kiss and the like — then divorced a second time in that pure period, it is not disliked. Yes, if he returned by intercourse then divorced, it is disliked because it is in a pure period in which intercourse occurred. [2] His saying: 'was approached' means she was not pregnant, not menopausal, and not a minor, as passed. [3] His saying: 'it is obligatory' means if he divorced during menstruation, he must return by intercourse after the end of menstruation or by word in it, to remove the sin. For this the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, ordered Ibn 'Umar when he divorced his wife during menstruation, narrated by al-Bukhari and others.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the matn of al-Wiqayah, expanded by the sharh. It addresses the conditions under which divorce is disliked or obligatory to revoke. The first part states that if a man divorces his wife twice in a single period of purity (tuhr) without having revoked the first divorce, or if he divorces her once in a tuhr where she was not approached, or if he divorces her during menstruation when she had been approached, then it is obligatory to revoke the divorce in the most correct position (al-asahh). Some Hanafi mashayikh consider it merely recommended (mustahab). The commentary clarifies: 'in a tuhr without revocability' applies to the second divorce — two divorces in one tuhr without intervening return. If the man divorces once, then returns by word or kiss, then divorces again in the same tuhr, it is not disliked. But if the return was by intercourse, then the second divorce is disliked because the tuhr was contaminated by intercourse. 'was approached' means the woman is not pregnant, menopausal, or a minor, as previously established. 'it is obligatory' refers to the case of divorcing during menstruation: the man must return to his wife after her menses ends, either by intercourse or by word, to lift the sin of divorcing in menstruation. This is based on the hadith where the Prophet ordered Ibn 'Umar to take back his wife when he divorced her during her period. The majority view (al-asahh) makes this return wajib, while some Hanafis hold it mustahab. The Hanafi school emphasizes that the command in the hadith indicates obligation unless evidence indicates recommendation.

Key Terms
طهر (tuhr): Period of purity between menstrual cycles, during which a woman is not menstruating.
رجعة (raj'ah): Revocation of a revocable divorce by word or action, returning the wife to marriage without a new contract.
موطوءة (mawtu'ah): A wife who has been sexually approached by her husband; in this context, one who is not a minor, menopausal, or pregnant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view (al-asahh) in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a husband returning to his wife after divorcing her during menstruation?
A) It is mustahab (recommended).
B) It is wajib (obligatory).
C) It is haram (forbidden).
D) The divorce is invalid, so no return is needed.

Key Takeaway
Divorcing during menstruation is a sin; the husband must return to his wife (raj'ah) after her menses ends, and this return is obligatory (wajib) according to the relied-upon Hanafi view.

The Hadith on Divorce: Reconciling Permissibility with Hatred
Exposition and critical analysis of the hadith on divorce's status

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that divorce is legally permissible (mubah) yet the most hated permissible act, and identify the basis for this ruling in the hadith.

Core Idea
Divorce is halal but most hated — permissibility is a legal ruling, hatred is an essential quality.

This lesson examines the famous hadith 'The most hated of lawful things to Allah is divorce' (Abu Dawood, Ibn Majah, al-Hakim). The Hanafi school upholds that divorce is permissible but severely disliked (makruh tanzihi). The commentary resolves the apparent contradiction between legal permission and divine hatred by distinguishing between the legal ruling and the inherent nature of the act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith and its implication
The hadith explicitly calls divorce 'the most hated of the lawful.' This suggests that while divorce is legally permitted, it is extremely displeasing to Allah.
2
Understand the hypothetical objection
One might ask how something can be both lawful and hated. This seems contradictory because 'lawful' implies approval, while 'hated' implies disapproval.
This objection is raised in the text exactly.
3
Recognize the Hanafi resolution
The commentary explains that permissibility (ibaha) is a legal ruling (hukm shar'i), while being hated (mabghudiyya) refers to the essence (dhat) of the act. They can coexist because the legal permissibility is granted for necessity despite the intrinsic dislike.
The phrase 'لا تنافي لأن الإباحة حكم شرعي، والمبغوضية ترجع إلى الذات' is the key.
4
Note the authenticity discussion
Several scholars critiqued the hadith's chain (mursal, narrators criticized), but it is widely accepted and acted upon. The Hanafi position relies on the meaning, even if the chain is debated.
This shows that figh rulings are not solely dependent on rigorous hadith authentication.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[٤] قوله : أبغض المباحات؛ الأصل فيه حديث : «أبغض الحلال إلى الله الطلاق» (٣)، أخرجه أبو داود وابن ماجة والحاكم. وفيه إشارة إلى أن الأصل في الطلاق الحظر، ويباح بل قد يستحب عند الحاجة. فإن قلت : كيف يكون الحلال مبغوضاً مع التنافي بين الحل أي الإباحة، وكونه مبغوضاً؟ قلت : لا تنافي؛ لأن الإباحة حكم شرعي، والمبغوضية ترجع إلى الذات، وقد يجتمعان، ألا ترى أن الطلاق يباح للحاجة مع كراهته. وعند الدارقطني : «ما خلق الله شيئاً أبغض إليه من الطلاق»)، وفيه إشارة إلى أن الأصل في الطلاق الحظر، ويباح بل قد يستحب عند الحاجة. فإن قلت : كيف يكون الحلال مبغوضاً مع التنافي بين الحل أي الإباحة، وكونه مبغوضاً؟ قلت : لا تنافي؛ لأن الإباحة حكم شرعي، والمبغوضية ترجع إلى الذات، وقد يجتمعان، ألا ترى أن الطلاق يباح للحاجة مع كراهته. وقال ابن حجر في فتح الباري (٩) : (٣٥٦) : أعل بالإرسال. وقال ابن عدي في الكامل» (٦ : ٤٦١) بعد ذكر الحديث : قال لنا أبو داود: فهذه سنة تفرد بها أهل الكوفة. وقول بن أبي داود تفرد بها أهل الكوفة : يعني رواه معرف بن واصل ؛ لأنه كوفي ولا أعلم رواه عن معرف إلا محمد بن خالد، قال الشيخ : ولا أعلم رواه عن معرف إلا محمد بن خالد ، ولمعرف غير ما ذكرت شيء يسير ، وهو ممن يكتب حديثه. وقال ابن الجوزي في العلل المتناهية (۲) : ٦٣٨) : هذا حديث لا يصح، ويحيى الوصافي ليس بشيء، قال الفلاس والنسائي : متروك الحديث». وتمام الكلام فيه في الحديث الذي يليه. (۱) في «المستدرك ٢ : ٢١٤)، و(سنن أبي داود (٢) : ٢٥٤) بلفظ : «ما أحل الله شيئاً أبغض إليه من الطلاق»، وقال الحاكم : وهذا حديث صحيح الإسناد لم يخرجاه، وقال في التمييز : روي موصولاً ومرسلاً وصحح البيهقي إرساله ، وكذا أبو حاتم ، وقال الخطابي : إنه المشهور. وله شاهد عند الدارقطني (٤) : (٣٥) ، والبيهقي (٧) : (٣٦١)، و«عبد الرزاق(٦ : معاذ الله مرفوعاً بلفظ : يا معاذ ما خلق الله شيئاً أحب إليه من العتاق ولا خلق الله عن شيئاً على وجه الأرض أبغض إليه من الطلاق ... الخ ، ورواه الديلمي في «الفردوس»(٥ : عن معاذ بلفظ : إن الله يبغض الطلاق ويحب العتاق، لكنه ضعيف بانقطاعه. وروى «الديلمي» (٢ : ٥١) عن أبي هريرة الله له أيضاً عن علي له رفعه بسند ضعيف : تزوجوا ولا تطلقوا ، فإن الطلاق يهتز منه العرش. وروي في «مصنف ابن أبي شيبة (٤) : (۱۸۷) عن علي الله أنه قال : يا أهل العراق لا تزوجوا الحسن ، يعني ابنه فإنه مطلاق. فقال له رجل: والله لتزوجنَّه فما رضي أمسكه وما كره طلق. وفي صحيح ابن حبان (۱۰) : (۸۲) و موارد الظمآن ۱ : ۳۲۱) : عن أبي موسى الله قال رسول : مـا بـال أحدكم يلعب بحدود الله ، يقول : قد طلقت ، قد راجعت». ينظر : كشف الخفاء» (۱ : ۲۸ - ٢٩)
[4] His saying: 'The most hated of permissible things'; its basis is the hadith: 'The most hated of the lawful to Allah is divorce,' narrated by Abu Dawood, Ibn Majah, and al-Hakim. It indicates that the original ruling on divorce is prohibition, but it becomes permissible, and even recommended at times of need. If you say: How can something lawful be hated, given the contradiction between being lawful (permissible) and being hated? I say: There is no contradiction; because permissibility is a legal ruling, and being hated refers to the essence, and they can coexist. Do you not see that divorce is permitted due to need despite its dislike. According to al-Daraqutni: 'Allah has not created anything more detestable to Him than divorce,' and it indicates that the original ruling on divorce is prohibition, but it becomes permissible, and even recommended at times of need. If you say: ... then answer... Al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar said in Fath al-Bari (9:356): It is declared defective by being mursal. Ibn 'Adiyy said in al-Kamil... Abu Dawood said: This is a sunnah unique to the people of Kufa. Ibn Abi Dawood's statement 'unique to the people of Kufa' means it was narrated by Ma'ruf ibn Wasi'; he is Kufan and I do not know anyone who narrated it from Ma'ruf except Muhammad ibn Khalid. Al-Shaykh said: I do not know anyone who narrated from Ma'ruf except Muhammad ibn Khalid. Ma'ruf has very few narrations besides what I mentioned, and his hadith are written. Ibn al-Jawzi said in al-'Ilal al-Mutanahiyya (2:638): This hadith is not authentic, and Yahya al-Wasifi is nothing; al-Fallas and al-Nasa'i said: He is abandoned. And the complete discussion on it is in the following hadith. ... [continues with chains and comments]
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage is a critical commentary on the hadith 'The most hated of the lawful to Allah is divorce.' The author begins by quoting the hadith from Abu Dawood, Ibn Majah, and al-Hakim, then notes that it implies the original ruling on divorce is prohibition (hazr), but it becomes permissible due to need, and even recommended. A hypothetical objection is raised: how can something lawful be hated? The answer is that permissibility is a legal ruling while being hated is a quality of the act itself; they can coexist, as divorce is permitted due to need despite its innate dislike. The author then extensively discusses the authenticity of the hadith, citing several scholars: Ibn Hajar al-Asqalani declared it mursal (incomplete chain). Ibn 'Adiyy quotes Abu Dawood saying it is a unique Kufan tradition with a weak chain. Ibn al-Jawzi deems it not authentic and criticizes a narrator. Al-Hakim considered it sahih, but al-Bayhaqi and others held it mursal. The author also provides supporting narrations, though they are weak. The lesson shows that while divorce is legally permissible, it is deeply disliked in the sight of Allah, and its original ruling in the Shari'ah would be prohibition were it not for the exceptional permission. The Hanafi school upholds this: divorce is mubah but makruh tanzihi; it becomes wajib or haram under certain circumstances.

Key Terms
أبغض الحلال (abghad al-halal): The most hated of the permissible things; a category showing that an act is legally permissible but severely detested by Allah.
الطلاق (al-talaq): The dissolution of marriage by the husband's pronouncement, subject to regulations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How do Hanafi scholars reconcile the hadith calling divorce 'the most hated of permissible things' with its permissibility?
A) They consider the hadith weak and therefore ignore it.
B) They say divorce is actually recommended, not hated.
C) They explain that permissibility is a legal ruling while hatred refers to the act's essence; they can coexist.
D) They interpret 'hated' to mean forbidden in all cases.

Key Takeaway
Divorce is legally permissible but spiritually detested; understanding this helps maintain the balance between legal flexibility and moral caution.
