فصل في إضافة الطلاق إلى الزمان
ويقع عند الفجر في أنتِ طالق غداً، أو في غد، وتصح نية العصر في الثاني فقط)، فإنَّه إذا قال : أنتِ طالق غداً، يقتضي أن تكون موصوفة بالطلاق في كلِّ الغد" فيقع عند الفجر، ولا تصح نيَّةَ العصر كما إذا قال : صمتُ السَّنةَ يدلُّ على أنه صام كلها بخلاف صمتُ في السنة.
[1] قوله : ويقع عند الفجر ؛ هي فجر الغد، قال الشارح له في «التنقيح» في بحث حروف المعاني»: «في للظرف، والفرقُ ثابت بين إثباته وإضماره، نحو: صمتُ هذه السنة، يقتضي الكل، بخلاف : صمتُ في هذه السنة، فلهذا في أنت طالق غداً يقعُ في أول النهار، ليكون واقعاً في جميع الغد، ولو قال : أنت طالق في الدار تطلق حالاً إلا أن ينوي في دخولك الدار، فيتعلّق به» [٢]قوله : نية العصر ؛ ذكره اتفاقي ، والمراد أنه لو نوى وقوعه في جزء خاص من أجزاء الغد غير الجزء الأول صح ذلك فيما إذا قال : في غد، ولا يصح ذلك فيما إذا قال غداً.
[٣] قوله : في كلّ الغد ؛ لأنَّ الظرف صار بمنزلة المفعول به منتصباً به، فيقتضي الاستيعاب كالمفعول به يقتضي تعلّق الفعل بمجموعه، ولو نوى في هذه الصورة آخر النهار صُدِّق ديانة لا قضاء ، وفي صورة ذكر «في» يصدق قضاء أيضاً ؛ لكونه نوى محتمل لفظه. كذا في «التلويح». [4] قوله : بخلاف صمت في السنة ؛ فإنه يصدق بصوم يوم من أيامها أيضاً، بل بصوم ساعة أيضاً، بأن ينوي الصوم إلى الليل ثمّ يفطر ؛ لأنَّ الظرف قد يكون أوسع. كذا في «التلويح»
[1] قوله : وفي قوله ... الخ ؛ حاصله : أن قوله : أنت طالق في غد لا يقتضي استيعاب الغد ؛ لأنّ الظرف لا يشترط فيه ذلك، فقد يكون أوسع من المظروف، بل يقتضي وقوع الطلاق في جزء من أجزاء الغد، بخلاف أنت طالق غداً، فإنّ المفعول فيه هناك شابه المفعول فيه فاقتضى الاستيعاب.
[٢]قوله : وليس جزء منه ... الخ ؛ دفع دخل مقدّر، تقرير الدخل : أنه لما كان مقتضاه وقوع الطلاق في جزء من أجزاء الغد: أي جزء كان، فما وجه تخصيص وقوعه بأول الجزء. وتحرير الدفع : أنّ ذلك ليس لاقتضاء الكلام خصوص وقوعه فيه، بل لأنه لَمَّا كان مقتضاه الوقوع في جزء من أجزائه، والأجزاء كلّها متساوية الأقدام، فلو أوقعناه في جزء دون جزء لزِمَ الترجيح من غير مُرَجّح ؛ فلذلك حكم بوقوعه في أول جزء منها ؛ الشرفه وسبقه وعدم مزاحمته الغير به.
[٣] قوله : تصح نيته ؛ أي قضاء وهذا عنده وعندهما : لا تصح كالأول، ولا خلاف في صحتها فيهما ديانة. والفرق لـه : عموم متعلّق «في» إذا كانت مقدّرة، دون ما إذا كانت ملفوظة ، للفرق لغة بين صمت سنة، وبين صمت في سنة، وشرعاً بين لأصومن عمري، حيث كله، وفي عمري ، حيث يبر بساعة. لا يبرأ إلا بصوم فنية جزء من الزمان عند ذكرها نية الحقيقة، ومع حذفها نية تخصيص العام، فلا يصدق قضاء، وهذا بخلاف ما لا يتجزأ الزمان في حقه، فإنّه لا فرق فيه بين حذف «في»، وبين إثباتها، كصمت يوم الجمعة، وصمتُ في يوم الجمعة. كذا في «البحر» و«النهر»
Section on attaching divorce to time: It occurs at dawn in 'you are divorced tomorrow' or 'in tomorrow', and the intention of Asr is valid only in the second. For when he says 'you are divorced tomorrow', it requires that she be described with divorce in all of tomorrow, so it occurs at dawn, and the intention of Asr is not valid, just as when he said 'I fasted the year' indicates that he fasted all of it, unlike 'I fasted in the year.' [1] His saying: 'It occurs at dawn' means the dawn of tomorrow. The commentator said in 'al-Tanqih' in the chapter on particles: 'Fi is for container, and the difference is established between its affirmation and omission, such as: I fasted this year requires the whole, unlike: I fasted in this year. Therefore, in 'you are divorced tomorrow' it occurs at the beginning of the day to be occurring in all of tomorrow. If he said 'you are divorced in the house', she is divorced immediately unless he intends 'upon your entering the house', then it is attached.' [2] His saying: 'Intention of Asr' is mentioned coincidentally, and the meaning is that if he intended its occurrence in a specific part of tomorrow other than the first part, that is valid when he said 'in tomorrow', but not when he said 'tomorrow'. [3] His saying: 'In all of tomorrow' because the container became like the object of the verb, requiring comprehensiveness like the object requires the attachment of the verb to its entirety. If he intended in this form the end of the day, he is believed religiously but not judicially. In the form mentioning 'fi', he is believed judicially also because he intended something his wording can bear. So in 'al-Talwih'. [4] His saying: 'Unlike I fasted in the year' because it is true with fasting one of its days, or even with fasting an hour, by intending fasting until night then breaking fast, because the container may be wider. So in 'al-Talwih'. [1] His saying: 'And in his saying...' etc: The summary is that his saying 'you are divorced in tomorrow' does not require encompassing tomorrow because the container does not require that; it may be wider than the contained. Rather, it requires the occurrence of divorce in a part of the parts of tomorrow, unlike 'you are divorced tomorrow' because the adverb resembles the object and thus requires comprehensiveness. [2] His saying: 'And no part of it is more entitled...' etc: This repels an implied objection. The objection: Since its requirement is the occurrence of divorce in a part of the parts of tomorrow, any part, what is the justification for specifying its occurrence at the first part? The answer: That is not because the speech requires its occurrence specifically at it, but because when its requirement is occurrence in a part of its parts, and all parts are equal in rank, if we placed it in a part without a part, it would require preferring without preference. Therefore, it is ruled to occur at the first part due to its honor, precedence, and lack of competition. [3] His saying: 'His intention is valid' i.e., judicially, and this is according to him (Abu Hanifa) while according to them (the two) it is not valid like the first, and there is no dispute about its validity religiously. The difference for him is the generality of the concerned object of 'fi' when it is implied, unlike when it is uttered, due to the linguistic difference between 'I fasted a year' and 'I fasted in a year', and legally between 'I will surely fast my life' where he must fast all of it, and 'in my life' where he can be absolved with an hour. He is not absolved except by fasting, except that when mentioning a part of time with the intention of the reality, and with its omission the intention of specifying the general, so he is not believed judicially. This is unlike what is not divisible time in its regard, where there is no difference between omitting and affirming 'fi', like 'I fasted Friday' and 'I fasted on Friday'. So in 'al-Bahr' and 'al-Nahr'.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of adding a time phrase to a divorce pronouncement. The matn states that when a husband says 'you are divorced tomorrow' (غداً) or 'in tomorrow' (في غد), the divorce occurs at the dawn of that day. The intention to have it at a specific time like Asr is valid only in the second phrasing. The commentary expands by explaining the linguistic reasoning: 'غداً' without the particle 'في' makes the time an adverb resembling a direct object, requiring the divorce to encompass the entire day (istī'āb). Thus it begins at the first moment to cover all. Intending a later part is not valid judicially (qadā'an), though it is accepted religiously (diyānatan). In contrast, 'في غد' treats 'tomorrow' as a mere container (zarf), implying only that divorce occurs in some part of it. Since all parts are equal, the divorce is placed at the first part to avoid arbitrary preference. Here, the intention of a specific part is valid judicially according to Abu Hanifa, but the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold it invalid like the first case. The difference stems from analogy to fasting: 'I fasted the year' means every day; 'I fasted in the year' allows a single day. For indivisible times like a single day, both phrasings are equivalent.

Key Terms
غداً (ghadan): An adverb meaning 'tomorrow' without the particle 'في', treated like a direct object requiring full temporal coverage.
في غد (fī ghadin): Phrase meaning 'in tomorrow' with the particle 'في', treating tomorrow as a container that can host a part.
نية (niyya): Intention of the husband to specify a particular time for divorce, e.g., Asr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) When the husband says 'أنت طالق غداً'
B) When the husband says 'أنت طالق في غد'
C) In both phrasings
D) In neither phrasing

Key Takeaway
The presence or absence of the particle 'في' determines whether judicial acceptance of time intention is possible in Hanafi divorce law.

Divorce in 'Fi Ghadd': Default Timing and the Intention Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on divorce timing with intention exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the default ruling that divorce occurs at fajr when a husband says 'أنت طالق في غد' and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the judicial effect of his intention to specify a different part.

Core Idea
Divorce in 'في غد' falls at fajr; intention only affects judicial ruling per Abu Hanifa.

This lesson tackles a classic Hanafi dispute about divorce tied to a future time. When a husband says 'You are divorced in tomorrow,' the phrase does not require the entire day to pass. But if every part is equal, which part triggers the divorce? The default answer is the first moment (fajr) to avoid arbitrary choice. However, what if the husband quietly intended a specific part, like noon? The Hanafi imams differ on whether that intention counts in court – a dispute with practical implications for judges and muftis alike.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core legal question
The phrase 'أنت طالق في غد' – does it require the divorce to occur across the whole day, or only in some part? The passage says it only requires a part, unlike 'أنت طالق غدا' which implies the whole day.
The preposition 'في' changes the scope.
2
Understand the default ruling without intention
Since the phrase requires only a part, and all parts are equal, assigning it to any specific part would be arbitrary (ترجيح بلا مرجح). To avoid that, the divorce is deemed to occur at the first moment (fajr) of the next day.
This is a rational proof (dalil aqli) based on the principle of avoiding preference without a preference-giver.
3
Introduce the intention exception
If the husband intended a specific part (e.g., noon), Abu Hanifa holds that his intention is valid judicially (qada), so the divorce falls at the intended time. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that intention does not affect the judicial ruling; the divorce still occurs at fajr. However, all agree it is valid religiously (diyanah) according to his intention.
The dispute hinges on the scope of 'في' and the role of hidden intention in court.
4
Trace the linguistic distinction
The passage explains that when 'في' is implied (as in 'أنت طالق غدا'), the time is encompassed; when explicit ('في غد'), only a part is needed. This parallels the difference between 'I fasted a year' (whole year) and 'I fasted in a year' (some part). For indivisible units like a single day, there is no difference.
This linguistic nuance is the basis for Abu Hanifa's position that intention can specify a part when 'في' is explicit.
5
Apply the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position for fatwa is that of the Sahibayn: intention is not effective judicially. The divorce always falls at fajr in court, regardless of the husband's secret intention. The intention matters only religiously.
This is the official stance of the later Hanafi school (Fatwa al-Hindiyya, Al-Hidayah sides with Sahibayn).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي قوله : أنتِ طالق في غدٍ يقتصي وقوعَ الطُلاقِ في جزء من الغد، وليس جزء منه" أولى من الجزء الآخر، فيقع عند الفجر ؛ لئلا يلزم الترجيح من غيرِ مرجح ، أما إذا نَوَى جزءا معينا تصح نيته (۳) [ ١ ] قوله : وفي قوله ... الخ ؛ حاصله : أن قوله : أنت طالق في غد لا يقتضي استيعاب الغد ؛ لأنّ الظرف لا يشترط فيه ذلك، فقد يكون أوسع من المظروف، بل يقتضي وقوع الطلاق في جزء من أجزاء الغد ، بخلاف أنت طالق غداً، فإنّ المفعول فيه هناك شابه المفعول فيه فاقتضى الاستيعاب. [٢]قوله : وليس جزء منه ... الخ ؛ دفع دخل مقدّر، تقرير الدخل : أنه لما كان مقتضاه وقوع الطلاق في جزء من أجزاء الغد: أي جزء كان، فما وجه تخصيص وقوعه بأول الجزء. وتحرير الدفع : أنّ ذلك ليس لاقتضاء الكلام خصوص وقوعه فيه، بل لأنه لَمَّا كان مقتضاه الوقوع في جزء من أجزائه، والأجزاء كلّها متساوية الأقدام، فلو أوقعناه في جزء دون جزء لزِمَ الترجيح من غير مُرَجّح ؛ فلذلك حكم بوقوعه في أول جزء منها ؛ الشرفه وسبقه وعدم مزاحمته الغير به. [٣] قوله : تصح نيته ؛ أي قضاء وهذا عنده وعندهما : لا تصح كالأول، ولا خلاف في صحتها فيهما ديانة. والفرق لـه : عموم متعلّق «في» إذا كانت مقدّرة، دون ما إذا كانت ملفوظة ، للفرق لغة بين صمت سنة، وبين صمت في سنة، وشرعاً بين لأصومن عمري، حيث كله، وفي عمري ، حيث يبر بساعة. لا يبرأ إلا بصوم فنية جزء من الزمان عند ذكرها نية الحقيقة، ومع حذفها نية تخصيص العام، فلا يصدق قضاء، وهذا بخلاف ما لا يتجزأ الزمان في حقه، فإنّه لا فرق فيه بين حذف «في»، وبين إثباتها، كصمت يوم الجمعة، وصمتُ في يوم الجمعة. كذا في «البحر»و«النهر»).
And in his statement: 'You are divorced in tomorrow' requires occurrence of divorce in a part of tomorrow, and no part is better than another, so it occurs at fajr to avoid preference without a preference-giver. However, if he intended a specific part, his intention is valid. [1] In summary: his statement 'You are divorced in tomorrow' does not necessitate encompassing tomorrow because the adverb does not require that, rather it necessitates occurrence in some part of tomorrow, unlike 'You are divorced tomorrow' where the adverb resembles the object and necessitates encompassing. [2] His saying 'and no part...' addresses a hypothetical objection: since it requires occurrence in any part, why specify the first? The answer is not because the statement specifies it, but because all parts are equal, so assigning it to any part without a preference-giver would be arbitrary; thus it occurs at the first part due to its honor and precedence. [3] His saying 'his intention is valid' means judicially; according to him (Abu Hanifa) it is valid, while according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is not valid like the first case, but there is no disagreement on its religious validity. The distinction for him is the general scope of 'fi' when it is implied, unlike when explicitly mentioned, based on the linguistic difference between 'I fasted a year' and 'I fasted in a year', and in Shari'ah between 'I swear to fast my whole life' where he fulfills the whole, and 'in my whole life' where he fulfills with one hour. He is not cleared except by fasting a specified part of time when 'fi' is mentioned, and when omitted it requires specification of the general, so it is not valid judicially. This is unlike where time is indivisible, where there is no difference between omitting and including 'fi', like 'I fasted Friday' and 'I fasted on Friday'.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling on divorce when the husband says 'You are divorced in tomorrow' (أنت طالق في غد). The commentator expands on the matn: the divorce falls at the first moment of tomorrow (fajr) because the phrase requires occurrence in some part, and no part is preferred over another; to avoid arbitrary selection (ترجيح بلا مرجح), it must occur at the earliest part. This is a rational proof (dalil aqli). However, if the husband intends a specific part of the day, his intention is valid judicially according to Abu Hanifa, but not according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), though all agree it is valid religiously (ديانة). The commentator then explains the linguistic distinction: when the preposition 'في' is implied (as in 'أنت طالق غدا' meaning 'tomorrow' without 'في'), the time is encompassed; when explicit ('في غد'), only a part is required. This mirrors the difference between 'I fasted a year' (encompassing) and 'I fasted in a year' (some part). For indivisible units like a day, there is no difference.

Key Terms
ظرف (zarf): Adverb of time here; in the phrase 'في غد', it indicates the time frame without requiring full coverage.
ترجيح بلا مرجح (tarjeeh bila murajjih): Arbitrary preference without a rational basis; avoided by assigning divorce to the earliest part.
نية (niyyah): Intention of the husband to specify a time part; affects judicial ruling only according to Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi position (Sahibayn), when does divorce occur if a man says 'أنت طالق في غد' without specifying a part?
A) At the end of the day
B) At the beginning (fajr) of the next day
C) At noon of the next day
D) It does not occur until the next day ends

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that 'في غد' triggers divorce at fajr, and secret intention cannot change the judicial decision, though it binds the husband religiously.

Ruling on Two-Time Divorce Phrases
Ruling on divorce when two times are mentioned

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a husband mentions two times for divorce and apply the rules depending on conjunction and order.

Core Idea
Divorce occurs at the earlier mentioned time; conjunction changes the count.

When a husband says 'You are divorced today tomorrow' or 'tomorrow today', the key legal question is: when does the divorce take effect? The Hanafi school provides a clear rule based on the earlier time mentioned and whether the times are joined by a conjunction. This lesson unpacks the logic using the text of 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the phrase type
Determine whether the two times are mentioned with or without a conjunction (e.g., 'and'). This distinction changes the ruling.
The phrase 'اليوم غداً' has no conjunction; 'اليوم وغداً' includes 'و'.
2
If no conjunction: locate the earlier time
Divorce occurs at the time mentioned first, regardless of whether it is present or future. The first word takes immediate effect for its time and suspends the second.
Example: 'طالق اليوم غداً' → divorce today. 'طالق غداً اليوم' → divorce tomorrow.
3
If with conjunction: examine order
When the times are joined by a conjunction (e.g., 'و'), the ruling depends on which time comes first. If present first ('اليوم وغداً'), only one divorce occurs immediately; if future first ('غداً واليوم'), two divorces occur: one conditional (future) and one immediate.
The logic: the present-time divorce renders the future divorce redundant; the future-time divorce does not negate the present.
4
Apply the rule to the scenario
Practice with given phrases from the text and verify your answers using the commentator's reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعند أولهما في اليوم غداً، أو غداً اليوم) : أي إن قال : أنت طالق اليوم غداً، يقعُ في اليوم، وإن قال : أنت طالق غداً اليوم، يقع في الغد. [١] قوله : وعند أولهما ... الخ ؛ يعني إذا ذكر للطلاق وقتين كائن ومستقبل، وقع الطلاق عند أولهما ذكراً كائناً كان أو مستقبلاً ؛ لأنه بذكر اللفظ الأول ثبت حكمه تنجيزاً في الأول وتعليقاً في الثاني، فلا يحتمل التغيير بذكرِ الثاني ؛ لأنَّ المنجز لا يقبلُ التعليق ولا المعلّق التنجيز. كذا في «البحر» (۱) وهذا إذا ذكر الوقتين بدون العطف، فإنّ ذكرهما بحرف العطف، فإن بدأ بالكائن اتحد الطلاق ووقع حالاً ، فإنّها إذا طلقت اليوم تكبون طالقـاً غداً، فلا حاجة إلى التعدد، وإن بدأ بالمستقبل تعدّد الطلاق، فيكون الأوّل معلّقاً . منجزاً، يقع حالاً. كذا في «التبيين»(۳)، و«البحر»(۳).
And according to the earlier of the two [times] in 'today tomorrow' or 'tomorrow today': i.e., if he says 'You are divorced today tomorrow', it occurs today; if he says 'You are divorced tomorrow today', it occurs tomorrow. [1] His saying 'and according to the earlier of the two' means if he mentions two times, present and future, divorce occurs at the earlier mentioned time, whether present or future, because by mentioning the first word, its ruling is established as immediate for the first and conditional for the second, and it cannot be changed by mentioning the second, because the immediate cannot become conditional nor the conditional immediate. This is when the two times are mentioned without conjunction. If mentioned with a conjunction, then if he starts with the present, the divorce is single and occurs immediately, because she is divorced today and becomes divorced tomorrow, so no need for multiplicity; if he starts with the future, it becomes two divorces: the first conditional, occurring at the arrival of the future, and the second immediate, occurring instantly.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn, expanded by the commentator. It addresses cases where the husband mentions two time references for divorce, such as 'أنت طالق اليوم غدا' (You are divorced today tomorrow) or 'أنت طالق غدا اليوم' (You are divorced tomorrow today). The ruling: divorce occurs at the earlier time mentioned. If he says 'today tomorrow', it occurs today; if 'tomorrow today', it occurs tomorrow. The reasoning is that the first word takes immediate effect (تنفيذ) for its time and suspends (تعليق) the second; the second cannot override the first. If the two times are joined by a conjunction (e.g., 'and'), then if the present time is mentioned first, only one divorce occurs immediately, because the woman is already divorced today, and the future phrase is superfluous. If the future is mentioned first, two divorces occur: one conditional upon the future (occurring when the time comes) and one immediate for the present.

Key Terms
كائن (ka'in): Present time (today) in the context of divorce timing.
مستقبل (mustaqbal): Future time (tomorrow) in the divorce phrase.
عطف ('atf): Conjunction (e.g., و) joining two time phrases, affecting the number of divorces.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband says 'أنت طالق غدا اليوم' (You are divorced tomorrow today), when does the divorce occur?
A) Today
B) Tomorrow
C) Both today and tomorrow
D) Neither, invalid

Key Takeaway
When two times are mentioned for divorce, the earlier time determines occurrence; conjunction with present-first yields one divorce, future-first yields two.

Void Divorce Utterances Attached to Impossible Times
Ruling on divorce phrases that are void due to temporal impossibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on divorce phrases that are temporally impossible and explain the proof from hadith.

Core Idea
A divorce uttered before marriage or before existence is void because the husband lacks the right to divorce at that time.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya addresses a classic scenario: a man says to his wife 'You are divorced before I marry you.' Is this effective? The commentator explains that such statements are لغو (void) as performative divorces because they attach to a time when no marital authority existed. We will examine the proof and the reasoning behind the rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is uttering 'You are divorced before I marry you' to one's wife. The ruling is that it is void (لغو) and no divorce occurs.
The voidness applies to the performative act of divorce, not to other possible interpretations.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith 'لا طلاق قبل النكاح' (No divorce before marriage) reported by the authors of the Sunan. This is a zanni al-thubut hadith but qati al-dalala for this ruling.
The hadith directly negates divorce before marriage.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith shows that divorce requires an existing marriage. The phrase 'before I marry you' contradicts this requirement; thus, the utterance cannot create a divorce. The phrase is performative (إنشاء), not informative (إخبار).
If the phrase were a report, it might be valid, but the voidness is specifically for the performative aspect.
4
Note the hypothetical objection and response
One might argue the phrase could be a kenning for no marriage or a report of a prior divorce. The commentator clarifies that the voidness is only in the performative sense, not as absolute voidness.
The objection is addressed to prevent misinterpretation.
5
Extend to additional examples
Similarly void phrases include 'You are divorced yesterday' (said on the wedding day), 'before I was created', 'before you were created', or 'while I was a boy/insane/asleep'. All these lack temporal validity or legal capacity.
These examples illustrate the principle that divorce requires both marital authority and capacity at the time of utterance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولغا أنت طالق قبل أن أتزوجك [٢] قوله : ولغا ... الخ ؛ أي إذا قال لزوجته: أنت طالق قبل أن أتزوجك يكون لغواً لا يقع به الطلاق ؛ لأنه أسنده إلى حالة منافية لمالكية الطلاق، فإنّه لا طلاق قبل النكاح ، كذا ورد عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم عند أصحاب السنن. فإن قلت : يحتمل أن يكون إخباراً عن عدم النكاح على سبيل الكناية، أو عن كونها مطلقة بتطليق زوج سابق ، فلا يكون لغواً. قلت : المراد من لغويّته لغويّته من حيث كونه إنشاء للطلاق لا مطلقاً، وكذا يصير لغواً قوله : لزوجته التي نكحها اليوم : أنت طالق أمس لما ذكرنا. [۳] قوله : أنت طالق ؛ وكذا أنت طالق قبل أن أخلق أو قبل أن تخلقي، أو طلقتك وأنا صبي أو مجنون أو نائم. كذا في «الدر المختار»(4).
And 'You are divorced before I marry you' is void. [2] His saying: 'and void' means if he says to his wife 'You are divorced before I marry you', it is void and no divorce occurs, because he attached it to a state contradictory to ownership of divorce, for there is no divorce before marriage. Thus it is narrated from the Prophet (ﷺ) by the authors of the Sunan. If you say: it could be an indication of no marriage by way of kenning, or of her being divorced by a previous husband, so it would not be void. I say: the intended voidness is as a performative utterance of divorce, not absolutely. Similarly, his statement to his wife whom he married today: 'You are divorced yesterday' becomes void for the same reason. [3] His saying: 'You are divorced' and similarly 'You are divorced before I was created' or 'before you were created', or 'I divorced you while I was a boy, insane, or sleeping.' Thus in al-Durr al-Mukhtar.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. The matn states that if a man says to his wife 'You are divorced before I marry you', it is void (لغو) and no divorce occurs. The commentator (مصنف) provides the proof: divorce requires an existing marriage (ملكية الطلاق), and this phrase refers to a time before marriage, so it is impossible. This is supported by the hadith reported in the Sunan: 'لا طلاق قبل النكاح' (No divorce before marriage). A hypothetical objection is raised: perhaps the statement is a report (إخبار) that he will not marry her, or that she was divorced by a prior husband. The commentator responds: the voidness pertains to the performative utterance (إنشاء) of divorce, not to other possible interpretations. Similarly, saying to a woman he married today 'You are divorced yesterday' is void. Additional examples include 'before I was created', 'before you were created', or 'I divorced you while I was a boy, insane, or asleep'—all invalid because the pronouncer lacked legal capacity or ownership at the time.

Key Terms
لغو (laghw): Void in the sense that the utterance does not produce legal effect as a divorce.
ملكية الطلاق (malikiyyat al-talaq): Ownership of the right to divorce; only exists within a valid marriage.
إنشاء (insha'): Performative utterance that creates a legal effect, as opposed to informative (إخبار).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man says to his wife: 'أنت طالق قبل أن أخلق' (You are divorced before I was created). What is the ruling?
A) Divorce occurs immediately
B) Divorce occurs when he is created (impossible)
C) The statement is void, no divorce
D) It is valid as a metaphor

Key Takeaway
A divorce utterance attached to a time before the husband's marital authority or legal capacity is void and ineffective.

Divorce with Two Time Expressions: 'Today Tomorrow' or 'Tomorrow Today'
Ruling with rational proof for divorce timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a husband says 'today tomorrow' or 'tomorrow today' in divorce, and explain the effect of using the conjunction 'wa'.

Core Idea
The divorce takes effect at the first mentioned time; the second time cannot change it, but a conjunction can make the second time into a separate divorce.

This lesson deals with a specific scenario in Islamic divorce: when the husband mentions two different times, such as 'today tomorrow' or 'tomorrow today'. The Hanafi school has clear rules based on whether the phrases are joined by 'and' or not. Understanding the concepts of immediate (munajjiz) and suspended (mu'allaq) divorce is key to applying these rules correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage discusses two main scenarios: when the two times are mentioned without a conjunction (e.g., 'today tomorrow') and when they are joined by 'wa' (and) (e.g., 'today and tomorrow').
Without conjunction, the first time dominates; with conjunction, the ruling changes.
2
Understand the rule without conjunction
If he says 'today tomorrow', the divorce occurs today. If he says 'tomorrow today', it occurs tomorrow. The first mentioned time determines the effect: present time gives immediate divorce, future time gives suspended divorce.
The second time is ignored because the immediate does not accept suspension and vice versa.
3
Analyze the reasoning
The first utterance establishes a ruling: if the time is present, it is immediate (munajjiz); if future, it is suspended (mu'allaq). The second utterance cannot change this because the nature of the first (immediate or suspended) is fixed.
This is a rational proof (dalil aqli) based on the nature of talaq.
4
Examine the rule with conjunction
If he uses 'wa' (and): starting with today ('today and tomorrow') results in one immediate divorce today (since she is divorced today, she is already divorced tomorrow). Starting with tomorrow ('tomorrow and today') results in two divorces: one suspended until tomorrow, and one immediate (today) for the second mention.
The conjunction changes the outcome because the second time is considered an independent utterance.
5
Apply to examples
Practice: given a phrase, decide when the divorce occurs and how many. E.g., 'you are divorced today tomorrow' → one divorce today. 'You are divorced tomorrow and today' → two divorces: one suspended until tomorrow and one immediate today.
Ensure you check for the presence of 'wa'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعند أولهما في اليوم غداً، أو غداً اليوم) : أي إن قال : أنت طالق اليوم غداً، يقع في اليوم، وإن قال : أنت طالق غداً اليوم، يقع في الغد.

[١] قوله : وعند أولهما ... الخ ; يعني إذا ذكر للطلاق وقتين كائن ومستقبل، وقع الطلاق عند أولهما ذكراً كائناً كان أو مستقبلاً ; لأنه بذكر اللفظ الأول ثبت حكمه تنجيزاً في الأول وتعليقاً في الثاني، فلا يحتمل التغيير بذكرِ الثاني ; لأن المنجز لا يقبل التعليق ولا المعلق التنجيز. كذا في «البحر» (۱) وهذا إذا ذكر الوقتين بدون العطف، فإن ذكرهما بحرف العطف، فإن بدأ بالكائن اتحد الطلاق وقع حالاً، فإنها إذا طلقت اليوم تكون طالقاً غداً، فلا حاجة إلى التعدد، وإن بدأ بالمستقبل تعدد الطلاق، فيكون الأول معلقاً منجزاً، يقع حالاً عند مجيء الغد، والثاني منجزاً. كذا في «التبيين»(۳)، و«البحر»(۳).
And at the first of them (two times) in 'today tomorrow' or 'tomorrow today': meaning if he says 'you are divorced today tomorrow', it occurs today, and if he says 'you are divorced tomorrow today', it occurs tomorrow. [1] His statement: 'And at the first of them...' etc.; meaning if he mentions for divorce two times, present and future, the divorce occurs at the first of them mentioned, whether present or future, because by mentioning the first utterance its ruling is established as immediate in the first and suspended in the second, so it does not admit change by mentioning the second, because the immediate does not accept suspension and the suspended does not accept immediacy. This is in al-Bahr. And this is if he mentions the two times without conjunction. If he mentions them with a conjunction, then if he begins with the present, the divorce is single and occurs immediately, because if she is divorced today she becomes divorced tomorrow, so there is no need for multiplicity. If he begins with the future, the divorce becomes multiple, so the first is suspended and immediate, occurring at the arrival of tomorrow, and the second is immediate. This is in al-Tibyan and al-Bahr.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with its proof. It explains that when a husband says 'you are divorced today tomorrow' (اليوم غداً), the divorce occurs today because the first mentioned time takes effect. Similarly, if he says 'tomorrow today' (غداً اليوم), it occurs tomorrow. The reason given is that the first utterance establishes the ruling as either immediate (if the time is present) or suspended (if the time is future). The second utterance cannot change this. If a conjunction (و) is used, the ruling changes: if he says 'today and tomorrow', only one divorce occurs immediately if he starts with today; if he starts with tomorrow, two divorces occur: one suspended until tomorrow and one immediate.

Key Terms
منجز (munajjiz): An immediate divorce that takes effect at the moment of utterance.
معلق (mu'allaq): A suspended divorce that takes effect upon fulfillment of a condition (here, arrival of a time).
عطف ('atf): Conjunction, especially using 'wa' (and) between two time expressions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband says to his wife 'أنت طالق غداً اليوم' (you are divorced tomorrow today), when does the divorce occur according to Hanafi fiqh?
A) Today
B) Tomorrow
C) Both today and tomorrow
D) Neither — it is void

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, when two times are mentioned without conjunction, the first time governs; with conjunction and starting with a future time, two divorces occur.

Ruling on Pronouncing Divorce Before Marriage
Ruling on impossible conditional divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a divorce pronounced before marriage is void and explain the legal rationale.

Core Idea
Divorce before marriage is void — the right to divorce requires ownership of the marital bond.

This passage clarifies that if a husband says to his wife 'you are divorced before I marry you', the pronouncement is legally void. It is not an informative statement but a failed performative act. The hadith 'no divorce before marriage' confirms this. The ruling also extends to other impossible conditions, such as 'before I was created' or 'while I was a child or insane.' Let's explore the reasoning and implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is a man saying to his wife (or a woman he is about to marry) 'you are divorced before I marry you'. The ruling is that this pronouncement is void (laghw) and produces no divorce.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith narrated by the authors of Sunan: 'لا طلاق قبل النكاح' (no divorce before marriage). This is a direct textual evidence.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but accepted in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Understand the rationale
The pronouncement is void because it is attached to a state that contradicts the ownership of divorce. A man does not own the right to divorce before marriage, as the marital bond does not exist.
Ownership of divorce (milk al-talaq) only arises after a valid marriage.
4
Address the potential objection
One might argue that the statement could be informative (e.g., alluding to no marriage or a past divorce). The commentary clarifies that its voidness is specifically regarding its performative (insha') aspect for divorce, not absolutely as a statement.
If intended as khabar, it may be truthful but does not effect divorce.
5
Note additional examples
Similar void pronouncements include: 'you are divorced before I was created', 'before you were created', 'I divorced you while I was a boy, insane, or asleep.' All are void because the condition is impossible or the person lacks capacity.
These examples reinforce the principle that impossibility or incapacity renders the divorce void.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولغا أنت طالق قبل أن أتزوجك [٢] قوله : ولغا ... الخ ; أي إذا قال لزوجته: أنت طالق قبل أن أتزوجك يكون لغواً لا يقع به الطلاق ; لأنه أسنده إلى حالة منافية لمالكية الطلاق، فإنه لا طلاق قبل النكاح، كذا ورد عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم عند أصحاب السنن. فإن قلت : يحتمل أن يكون إخباراً عن عدم النكاح على سبيل الكناية، أو عن كونها مطلقة بتطليق زوج سابق، فلا يكون لغواً. قلت : المراد من لغويته لغويته من حيث كونه إنشاء للطلاق لا مطلقاً، وكذا يصير لغواً قوله : لزوجته التي نكحها اليوم : أنت طالق أمس لما ذكرنا. [٣] قوله : أنت طالق ; وكذا أنت طالق قبل أن أخلق أو قبل أن تخلقي، أو طلقتك وأنا صبي أو مجنون أو نائم. كذا في «الدر المختار»(4).
And 'you are divorced before I marry you' is void. [2] His statement: 'And void...' etc.; meaning if he says to his wife: 'you are divorced before I marry you', it is void, no divorce occurs, because he attached it to a state that contradicts ownership of divorce, for there is no divorce before marriage. Thus it is narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him) by the authors of the Sunan. If you say: It is possible that it is an informative statement about the absence of marriage by way of allusion, or about her being divorced by a previous husband's divorce, so it would not be void. I say: The intended meaning of its voidness is its voidness in terms of being a performative utterance of divorce, not absolutely. And similarly, his statement to his wife whom he married today: 'you are divorced yesterday' becomes void for what we mentioned. [3] His statement: 'you are divorced'; and likewise 'you are divorced before I was created' or 'before you were created', or 'I divorced you while I was a boy or insane or asleep.' This is in al-Durr al-Mukhtar.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage is a ruling supported by a hadith evidence. It establishes that if a husband says to his wife 'you are divorced before I marry you', the pronouncement is void and no divorce occurs. The reason is that there is no marital relationship before marriage, so the husband does not possess the right to divorce. The hadith 'no divorce before marriage' is cited. The commentary addresses an objection: perhaps it could be an informative statement? It clarifies that it is void as a performative divorce, not as a statement. Additional examples are given: saying 'before I was created', 'before you were created', or 'when I was a boy, insane, or asleep' are similarly void.

Key Terms
لغو (laghw): Void, ineffective; a pronouncement that does not produce legal effect.
إنشاء (insha'): A performative utterance that creates a legal effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Immediate Divorce Upon Silence After Conditional Phrases
Explaining that saying 'you are divorced unless I divorce you' and remaining silent causes immediate divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling that using 'ma lam' conditional phrases in divorce followed by silence triggers immediate divorce and determine the number of divorces that occur.

Core Idea
If a husband says 'you are divorced unless I divorce you' and remains silent, the divorce occurs immediately because the temporal condition is fulfilled.

In Hanafi fiqh, certain phrases like 'you are divorced as long as I do not divorce you' create a conditional divorce that is tied to time. Silence after such a statement is not mere inaction; it is legally significant as the fulfillment of the condition. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof from the Quran, and how to determine the number of divorces that take effect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditional phrases
The passage lists phrases: 'you are divorced as long as I do not divorce you' (ما لم أطلقك), 'when I do not divorce you' (متى لم أطلقك), and 'whenever I do not divorce you' (متى ما لم أطلقك). These all express a temporal condition – the divorce is suspended upon a time that is devoid of an actual divorce from him.
The key element is the use of time-related words like 'ma' (as long as), 'mata' (when).
2
Understand the linguistic proof
The Hanafi proof comes from the Quranic verse (Maryam 31) where 'ma dumtu hayyan' means 'as long as I am alive'. The word 'ma' here denotes time. By analogy, 'ma lam utalliqki' means 'as long as I do not divorce you'. Thus silence – the absence of a divorce from him – fulfills the condition, and the divorce takes effect.
This is a dalil naqli from Quran and a linguistic analysis that 'ma' is a zarf al-zaman (adverb of time).
3
Interpret 'silence' correctly
The passage clarifies that 'sakata' (remained silent) does not mean absolute silence but silence specifically about divorce. If the husband speaks other words after the conditional phrase, the condition is still fulfilled (since he didn't divorce), and divorce still occurs. The important point is that he does not utter a divorce during the time period.
This nuance prevents misunderstanding that only total silence triggers the ruling.
4
Determine the number of divorces
The number of divorces that occur depends on his specification: if he said 'three', three divorces occur making her irrevocably divorced; if 'two', two occur; if unrestricted, one divorce occurs and no further divorce can be added by this statement.
If he said 'you are divorced as long as I do not divorce you' without a number, only one divorce takes effect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي أنتِ كذا ما لم أطلقك، أو متى لم أطلقك، أو متى ما لم أطلقك، وسكت يقع حالاً [٣] قوله : وفي أنت كذا ... الخ، وجد وقوع الطلاق في الحال في هذه الصور على ما في كتب الأصول إن كلمة : متى و متى ما من ظروف الزمان، صريحان في الوقت، وكذا كلمة ما تجيء للوقت، كما في قوله تعالى حكاية عن قول سيدنا عيسى عليه السلام: وَأَوْصَانِي بِالصَّلَاةِ وَالزَّكَاةِ مَا دُمْتُ حَيًّا (مريم:31)، فلما أضاف الطلاق إلى زمان خال عن التطليق وسكت، وجد زمان خال عن التطليق، فيقع فيه الطلاق. [٤] قوله : وسكت ; ليس المراد به السكوت مطلقاً وترك التكلم مطلقاً، فإنه لو تكلم بكلام آخر متصلاً بجملة طلاقه يقع الطلاق أيضاً لوجود الزمان الخالي عن التطليق، بل المراد به السكوت عن الطلاق، وهذا احتراز عما لو قال : أنت ما لم أطلقك أنت طالق، وسيجيء حكمه. [٠] قوله : يقع حالاً ; أي بمجرد سكوته، فإن كان قيده بالثلاث حرمت عليه حتى تنكح زوجاً غيره، وإن قيده باثنتين وقعتا، وإن أطلق وقعت واحدة، ثم لا تقع أخرى، (١) مريم : من الآية ٣١.
And in 'you are (divorced) as long as I do not divorce you', or 'when I do not divorce you', or 'whenever I do not divorce you', and he remains silent, it occurs immediately. [3] His statement: 'And in you are such...' etc., the occurrence of divorce immediately in these forms is established according to the books of usul, because the word 'mata' and 'mata ma' are adverbs of time, explicit in time, and likewise the word 'ma' comes for time, as in His statement quoting our master Jesus (peace be upon him): 'And He enjoined upon me prayer and zakah as long as I am alive' (Maryam 31). So when he attached divorce to a time devoid of divorce and remained silent, a time devoid of divorce was found, so divorce occurs in it. [4] His statement: 'and remained silent' does not mean absolute silence and leaving speech absolutely, because if he speaks other speech connected to his divorce sentence, the divorce also occurs due to the existence of time devoid of divorce, rather it means silence about divorce. This is a caution against his saying 'you are divorced unless I divorce you' and its ruling will come. [0] His statement: 'it occurs immediately' means at the moment of his silence. So if he restricted it with three, she becomes unlawful for him until she marries another husband; if he restricted with two, they occur; if he released it (unrestricted), one occurs, then no other occurs.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage explains that if a husband uses phrases like 'you are divorced as long as I do not divorce you', 'when I do not divorce you', or 'whenever I do not divorce you', and then remains silent (i.e., does not divorce her), the divorce occurs immediately upon silence. The proof is from usul: the words 'mata' and 'ma' are used for time, as in the Quran (Maryam 31). Since he attached divorce to a time when divorce is not happening, and silence proves that time has arrived, the divorce takes effect. The commentary clarifies that 'silence' here means silence about divorce specifically, not total silence. If he speaks other words, the divorce still occurs. The number of divorces depends on his specification: if he said three, three occur; if two, two; if unspecified, one occurs and no further.

Key Terms
ظرف الزمان (zarf al-zaman): Adverb of time; words like 'mata' and 'ma' that specify time.
سكوت (sukut): Silence; specifically silence about divorce in this context.
تطليق (tatliq): Act of divorcing; pronouncing divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A husband says 'you are divorced as long as I do not divorce you' (أنت طالق ما لم أطلقك) and then remains silent. According to Hanafi fiqh, what is the outcome?
A) No divorce occurs because he did not explicitly divorce her.
B) One divorce occurs immediately upon silence.
C) Three divorces occur immediately.
D) It is considered a metaphor and no divorce occurs.

Key Takeaway
Silence after a temporal conditional divorce phrase is legally equivalent to fulfilling the condition, causing an immediate divorce in Hanafi law.

Particles in Suspended Divorce: Temporal vs Conditional
Ruling on timing of divorce with conditional/temporal particles

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between temporal and conditional particles in divorce pronouncements and apply the Hanafi rule to determine when divorce takes effect.

Core Idea
The particle determines timing: 'In' delays divorce to death; temporal particles cause immediate divorce.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains the critical distinction between conditional and temporal particles in suspended divorce. The Hanafi school holds that the linguistic meaning of the particle directly affects when the divorce takes effect. Understanding this distinction prevents errors in applying rulings on suspended divorces.

Guided Path
1
Identify the particle used
The text examines 'In', 'Idha', 'Mata', and 'Ma lam'. Determine whether the particle is purely conditional or incorporates temporal meaning.
Particles: 'In' (pure condition), 'Mata' (time only), 'Idha' (condition+time), 'Ma lam' (duration).
2
Analyze the linguistic function
According to Hanafi usul, 'In' is for pure condition (uncertainty), 'Mata' is for time only, 'Idha' combines condition and time, 'Ma lam' indicates duration.
The Quranic usage of 'In' for doubtful contexts supports the Hanafi view.
3
Apply the ruling
For each particle, decide when the divorce occurs: immediately upon silence or at the end of life.
For 'In', divorce occurs at death; for 'Mata', immediately; for 'Idha', Abu Hanifah says like 'In' (end of life) if no intention.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifah treats 'Idha' and 'Idhama' without intention as pure condition; the Sahibayn consider them temporal. Understand the practical difference.
The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifah's.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Abu Hanifah's view divorce is delayed to end of life; under the Sahibayn it would be immediate, affecting remarriage and iddah.
This difference has significant practical consequences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأنتِ طالق أمس لمن نكحها اليوم، ويقعُ الآن فيمن نَكَحَ قبل أمس، وفي أنتِ كذا ما لم أطلقك ، أو متى لم أطلقك ، أو متى ما لم أطلقك، وسكت يقع حالاً. وفي إن لم أطلقك يقع في آخر عمره. وإذا وإذاما بلا نية مثل : إن ؛ عند أبي حنيفة. نعم لو قال : كلما لم أطلقك فأنت طالق وسكت وقعت الثلاث إن كانت مدخولة. كذا في «النهر». قوله : في آخر عمره ؛ هذا إن مات قبلها ، وإن ماتت قبله ففي آخر جزء من أجزاء حياتها، والوجه في ذلك على ما فصله في «التلويح» وغيره : أنّ كلمة «إن» موضوعة للشرط ؛ أي لتعليق مضمون جملة بحصولِ مضمون جملة أخرى فقط ، من غير اعتبار ظرفية، كما في «إذا» و «متى»، فإنَّ «متى» تستعمل في الظرفية خاصة من دون اعتبار الشرط. و«إذا» مستعمل للشرط مع الظرفية، وتدخلُ إن على متردّد الوجود بين أن يكون وبين أن لا يكون، ولا تستعمل فيما هو قطعي الوجود ، ولا فيما هو قطعي الانتفاء إلا على تنزيله منزلة المشكوك لنكتة ، كما في قوله : وَإِن كُنتُمْ فِي رَيْبٍ مِّمَّا نَزَّلْنَا عَلَى عَبْدِنَا فَأْتُوا بِسُورَةٍ مِّن مِثْلِهِ، وقوله : لَينَ أَشْرَكْتَ لَيَحْطَنَّ عَمَلكَ ) ففي قوله : أنت طالق إن لم أطلقك ما داما حيين يمكن أن يطلقها فلا يقعُ المعلق على عدم التطليق، وإنما يتحقق ذلك في آخر حياة الزوج أو الزوجة، فيقع عند ذلك. الحياة عاجز عن التكلم بالطلاق، ووقوع المعلّق يشترط له القدرة عليه.
And 'You are divorced yesterday' for a woman he married today, and it takes effect now for the one he married before yesterday. And in 'You are such unless I divorce you', or 'when I do not divorce you', or 'whenever I do not divorce you', and he remains silent, it takes effect immediately. And in 'If I do not divorce you', it takes effect at the end of his life. And 'Idha' and 'Idhama' without intention are like 'In' according to Abu Hanifah. Yes, if he says 'Every time I do not divorce you, you are divorced' and remains silent, three divorces occur if she was consummated with. Thus in 'al-Nahr'. His statement: 'at the end of his life' – this if he dies before her, and if she dies before him, then at the last part of her life. The reasoning for that, as detailed in 'al-Talwih' and others: that the word 'In' is placed for condition; i.e. for suspending the content of a clause upon the occurrence of another clause only, without consideration of temporality, unlike 'Idha' and 'Mata'. Indeed, 'Mata' is used for temporality alone without consideration of condition. And 'Idha' is used for condition along with temporality. And 'In' enters upon something whose existence is uncertain between being and not being, and is not used for what is definitely existent nor for what is definitely non-existent except by treating it as doubtful for a reason, as in His saying: 'If you are in doubt about what We have sent down to Our servant, then bring a Surah like it' and His saying: 'If you associate others with Allah, your work will surely become worthless.' So in his saying 'You are divorced if I do not divorce you', as long as both are alive, he can divorce her, so the suspended [divorce] upon not divorcing does not occur, and that is only realized at the end of the life of the husband or wife, so it occurs then. [Because] life is unable to speak divorce, and the occurrence of the suspended condition requires ability upon it.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage from the commentary expands on the rules of adding divorce to time. It first explains a scenario where a man says 'You are divorced yesterday' to a woman he married today. If he married her today, the divorce cannot apply to yesterday, so it takes effect immediately (now). But if he married her before yesterday, then 'yesterday' is a valid time after marriage, but since one cannot create a divorce in the past, it also takes effect immediately. The text then discusses conditional phrases: 'unless I divorce you', 'when I do not divorce you', etc. If the husband says these and remains silent (i.e., does not divorce her), the divorce falls immediately because the condition of not divorcing is met at that moment. The word 'Mata' (when) and 'Mata ma' indicate time, so the divorce attaches to that time. For the phrase 'If I do not divorce you' (using particle 'In'), the ruling is different: it takes effect only at the end of his life (or her life if she dies first). This is because 'In' is a pure conditional particle without temporal meaning; the condition 'I do not divorce you' is not realized until death, after which divorce is impossible. An intra-Hanafi dispute is mentioned: Abu Hanifah rules that 'Idha' and 'Idhama' without intention are treated like 'In' (pure condition), while the two students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) likely consider them temporal, causing immediate effect. The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifah's. The passage also notes that if he says 'Every time I do not divorce you,' three divorces occur immediately because repetition is implied.

Key Terms
إضافة الطلاق إلى الزمان (Idafat al-talaq ila al-zaman): Attaching the pronouncement of divorce to a specific time, whether past, future, or conditional.
إن (In): A conditional particle indicating pure condition without temporal meaning; used for uncertain events.
ما لم أطلقك (Ma lam utalliqki): A phrase meaning 'as long as I have not divorced you' or 'unless I divorce you', treated as a temporal condition that, if left without action, triggers immediate divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A husband says to his wife: 'You are divorced if I do not divorce you' (using the particle 'In') and remains silent. When does the divorce occur according to Abu Hanifah?
A) Immediately upon his silence
B) At the end of his life or her life (whichever comes first)
C) Only if he explicitly says 'I divorce you' afterwards
D) Not at all, because the condition is impossible

Key Takeaway
The particle used in a suspended divorce determines the timing: pure condition ('In') delays to death; temporal particles cause immediate effect.

The Word 'Idha' in Conditional Divorce: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the word 'idha' in conditional divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute over the word 'idha' in conditional divorce, identify the respective proofs, and state the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
A single word 'idha' can change the timing of divorce: Abu Hanifa defers, Sahibayn apply immediately.

The word 'idha' (إذا) in Arabic can mean 'when' (time) or 'if' (condition). When a husband says 'idha lam utalliquk' without clarifying his intention, the Hanafi school is divided on whether the divorce occurs immediately or only after a delay. This lesson unpacks the grammatical and legal reasoning behind this ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ambiguous statement
The husband says 'idha lam utalliquk' (if/when I do not divorce you). The word 'idha' is the key. Without intention, does it mean 'whenever I do not divorce you' (immediate) or 'if I do not divorce you' (conditional)?
2
State the two Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa: 'idha' is shared (mushtarak) between time and condition. Since it is ambiguous, the divorce does not occur immediately; it is suspended until the end of life or unless intention clarifies. Sahibayn: 'idha' is literal for time; it means 'whenever', so the divorce occurs immediately upon utterance.
3
Analyze the grammatical basis
The dispute originates from Kufan (shared meaning) vs. Basran (literal for time) grammar schools. The Sahibayn adopt the Basran view, and later Hanafi authorities (e.g., Fath al-Qadir) prefer it.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position for fatwa is that of the Sahibayn: the divorce occurs immediately. This is the view preferred by al-Marghinani and later commentators.
5
Distinguish from delegation (tafwid)
In delegation ('Divorce yourself when you wish'), the wife's authority to divorce is clear, so doubt does not remove it. In conditional divorce, the divorce itself is uncertain, so doubt prevents its occurrence until clarified.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعندهما كمتى، ومع نية الوقت ، أو الشرط فكنيته) : فهذا بناء على أنّ : إذا ؛ عند أبي حنيفة له مشترك بين الشرط والظرف. وعندهما حقيقة في الظرف، وقد تجيء للشرط بطريق المجاز". قلت : وقوع الطلاق المعلّق بهذا الشرط عند وجود الشرط أمر حكمي، فلا يشترط له ما يشترط الحقيقة التطليق، بل يكتفي بالقدرة عند التعليق». [١]قوله : ومع نية ... الخ ؛ يعني إن نوى بإذا لم أطلقك وقت عدم تطليقه، أو نوى معنى الشرط ، كأن تعتبر بنيته، ويحكم بحسبها ؛ لأنها تحتمل كليهما، ونية المحتمل معتبرة، وهذا اتفاقي، وإنما الخلاف بينه وبينهما فيما إذا لم ينو شيئاً. [٢]قوله : مشترك ... الخ ؛ هذا هو مذهب الكوفيين من النحاة، فإنهم قالوا: قد تستعمل «إذا» للظرف، بمعنى وقتِ حصول ما أضيف إليه، فلا يحرم به الفعل، ويكون استعماله فيهما هو قطعي الوجود. وقد تستعمل للشرط بمعنى تعليق حصول مضمون جملة بحصول مضمون جملة أخرى، ويجزم به المضارع، ويكون استعماله في أمر على خطر الوجود مثل أن قوله حقيقة، هذا هو مذهب البصريين ، ورجّحه في «فتح القدير»، وغيره. [٣] قوله : بطريق المجاز ؛ لكن لا يسقط عنه معنى الظرف، صرح به الشارح الله في «التنقيح»(۳). وأورد عليه : أنه يلزم حينئذ الجمع بين الحقيقة والمجاز. وأجيب عنه : بأنه على سبيل عموم المجاز، حيث استعمل اللفظ الموضوع للوقتِ في مجموع الوقت والشرط. وفيه أنه لا يجوز إطلاق الأرض مثلاً على مجموع السماء والأرض، وليس هذا من عموم المجاز. فالحق في الجواب أن يقال: إنّها لم تستعمل إلا في معنى الظرف، لكن تضمنت معنى الشرط باعتبار إفادة الكلامِ تقييد حصولِ مضمون جملة بمضمون جملة، بمنزلة المبتدأ المتضمن لمعنى الشرط ، ولا يلزم من ذلك استعمال اللفظ في غير ما وضع له. كذا حققه التفتازاني له في «التلويح (۲)، ولعلّك أن تتفطن من هاهنا ما في كلام الشارح ه هاهنا من المسامحة. [1] قوله : كما إذا قال ؛ يعني إذا قال الرجلُ مخاطباً لامرأته : طلقي نفسك إذا شئت، كان بمنزلة : متى شئت في أنّه لا تتقيّد المشيئة في المجلس، بخلاف إن شئت، فإنّ المشيئة هناك متعلّقة بالمجلس، لا تتجاوز عنها، كما سيأتي تفصيله في موضعه إن شاء الله تعالى. [٢] قوله : فلا يقع بالشك ؛ لأن الطلاق غير واقع، وما هو غير واقع لا يقع بالشك، بخلاف مسألة المشيئة فإنّ أمرها فوض إليها بقوله : طلّقي نفسك قطعاً، فلا يزول بالشك. [۳] قوله : وأما مسألة المشيئة ؛ جواب عمّا استشهد به أبو يوسف ومحمد صلى الله عليه وسلم ببيان الفرق، وملخصه أن الأصل عدمُ الطلاق فلا يقع بالشك، وفي التفويض الأصل الاستمرار فلا ينقطع بالشك.
And according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is like 'whenever' (mata), and if he intends the time or the condition, then according to his intention. This is based on the fact that 'idha' according to Abu Hanifa is shared between condition and time. According to them (the Sahibayn), it is literal for time, and it may come for condition metaphorically. I say: The occurrence of conditional divorce with this condition upon the existence of the condition is a legal matter; thus what is required for an actual divorce is not required for it; rather, capacity at the time of suspension suffices. [1] His saying: 'And with intention...' means if he intends by 'idha' the time of not divorcing her, or intends the meaning of condition, he is judged according to his intention because it can bear both meanings, and the intention of what is probable is considered. This is agreed upon; the dispute between him and them is only when he does not intend anything. [2] His saying: 'shared...' This is the doctrine of the Kufan grammarians; they said that 'idha' is sometimes used for time, meaning the time of occurrence of what it is added to, so it does not govern the verb, and its use in both is definitive. And it is sometimes used for condition, meaning suspending the occurrence of the content of one clause upon the occurrence of the content of another clause, and it governs the present tense as jussive. Its use in a matter that is at risk of existence is like his saying... literally; this is the doctrine of the Basrans, and it was preferred in 'Fath al-Qadir' and others. [3] His saying: 'metaphorically'; but it does not lose its temporal meaning; the commentator stated it in 'al-Tanqih'. An objection was raised: that this necessitates combining literal and metaphorical. It was answered: that it is in the way of general metaphor, where the word placed for time is used for the combination of time and condition. There is an issue: it is not permissible to say 'earth' for the combination of sky and earth; this is not an instance of general metaphor. The correct answer is to say: It is only used in the meaning of time, but it includes the meaning of condition by virtue of the statement indicating the restriction of the content of one clause to the content of another clause, similar to the subject (mubtada) that includes the meaning of condition; this does not entail using the word in other than what it was placed for. This is what al-Taftazani verified in 'al-Talwih'. Perhaps you will notice here what is in the commentator's words of lenience. [1] His saying: 'as when he says' means if a man says to his wife: 'Divorce yourself when you wish', it is like 'whenever you wish' in that the wish is not restricted to the session, unlike 'if you wish', where the wish is tied to the session and does not extend beyond it, as will be detailed in its place if Allah wills. [2] His saying: 'so it does not occur with doubt' because the divorce is not occurring, and what is not occurring does not occur with doubt; contrary to the issue of delegation (tafwid) where her matter is entrusted to her definitively by his saying 'Divorce yourself', so it does not cease with doubt. [3] His saying: 'As for the issue of delegation' is a response to what Abu Yusuf and Muhammad used as evidence, clarifying the difference. Its summary: The principle is the absence of divorce, so it does not occur with doubt; and in delegation the principle is continuity, so it does not cease with doubt.
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the word 'idha' used in conditional divorce. The author clarifies the ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). The issue arises when a husband says to his wife, 'If I do not divorce you (idha lam utalliquk),' and then divorces her after some time. The ruling depends on the interpretation of 'idha'. According to Abu Hanifa, 'idha' is a homonym (mushtarak) between meaning time (zarf) and condition (shart). Therefore, if the husband does not specify his intention, it is ambiguous. Since divorce is a serious matter, the default is non-occurrence; thus the divorce does not take place in the present (hal). According to the Sahibayn, 'idha' is literally (haqiqa) for time, and only metaphorically (majaz) for condition. Therefore, when the husband says 'idha lam utalliquk', it means 'whenever I do not divorce you' (mata lam utalliquk), so the divorce occurs immediately upon utterance. The author explains that the dispute is built on a grammatical difference: the Kufans (Abu Hanifa's school) held 'idha' to be shared, while the Basrans (the grammarian basis for Sahibayn) held it to be literal for time. The text then refines this: the preferred view, as in 'Fath al-Qadir', is that 'idha' is literal for time but includes a conditional meaning. Furthermore, the author distinguishes this case from the case of delegation (tafwid), where the husband says 'Divorce yourself when you wish.' In delegation, there is no doubt about the authorization, so the wife's power to divorce remains even if she doubts. In conditional divorce, there is no established divorce, so doubt prevents occurrence. The practical consequence (thamara) is that when the husband says 'idha lam utalliquk' without intention, Abu Hanifa rules that the divorce does not occur upon the condition (i.e., when he does not divorce her over time), but rather at the end of his life or not at all? Actually, the text says: if 'idha' is intended as 'mata', it occurs in the present; if as 'in' (condition), it occurs at the end of life. Since there is doubt, it does not occur in the present according to Abu Hanifa. The Sahibayn rule it occurs immediately. The mufta bihi position is that of the Sahibayn, as preferred in 'Fath al-Qadir' and 'al-Bahr al-Ra'iq'.

Key Terms
إذا (idha): A Arabic particle; according to Abu Hanifa it is shared between time and condition; according to Sahibayn it is literal for time and metaphorical for condition.
شرط (shart): Condition: a stipulation that suspends the occurrence of a legal consequence (like divorce) upon the occurrence of a future event.
ظرف (zarf): Time or place; here specifically temporal meaning as an adverb of time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi Hanafi position, if a husband says 'idha lam utalliquk' without intention, when does the divorce occur?
A) It does not occur at all until the husband explicitly divorces her again.
B) It occurs immediately upon utterance.
C) It occurs at the end of the husband's life.
D) It occurs only if the husband never divorces her during his lifetime.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school internally disputes the meaning of 'idha' in conditional divorce, but the relied-upon position is that divorce occurs immediately, based on the literal temporal meaning.

Conditional Divorce Followed by Immediate Divorce
Ruling on the effect of a conditional divorce immediately followed by an unconditional divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of istihsan to determine the effect of a conditional divorce immediately followed by an unconditional divorce.

Core Idea
When a conditional divorce is immediately followed by an unconditional divorce, only the unconditional takes effect because the time of fulfilling the oath is exempted from the condition.

This passage presents a nuanced scenario in divorce law: a husband pronounces a conditional divorce and then, without pause, an unconditional divorce. The central question is whether both divorces occur or only the second. The Hanafi school, relying on istihsan (juristic preference), rules that only the immediate divorce takes effect. In this lesson, we will unpack the reasoning, examine the qiyas counterargument from Zufar, and understand the practical consequences for the number of divorces that fall.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario and the Two Utterances
The husband says 'أنت طالق ما لم أطلقك' (conditional) then immediately 'أنت طالق' (unconditional) without a significant pause. Recognize the two components: a suspended divorce (mu'allaqa) and an immediate divorce (munajjaz).
The text stresses the continuity (ittisal) between the two pronouncements.
2
State the Hanafi Position from the Matn
According to the matn and its commentary, the divorce takes effect by the last utterance—the unconditional one—only. The first conditional divorce does not occur because the condition is immediately overridden.
The sharh explicitly says 'تطلق بالأخيرة' (she becomes divorced by the last).
3
Understand the Qiyas Objection (Zufar's View)
By strict analogy (qiyas), there exists a brief moment between the two statements that is free of any divorce (the time before the second utterance is completed). Zufar argued that during that moment the condition remains possible, so both divorces should apply.
Zufar is an early Hanafi scholar; his view is recorded but not relied upon.
4
Apply the Istihsan Argument
The relied-upon reasoning is istihsan: the time of fulfilling the oath (birr) is exempted from the condition by contextual evidence (dalalat al-hal). The husband's immediate pronouncement indicates his intention to fulfill the condition (i.e., to effect a divorce contrary to the suspension). This exemption overrides the strict qiyas.
An example is given: if someone swears not to live in a house and immediately begins moving out, the oath is considered fulfilled.
5
Analyze Practical Consequences (Thamarah al-Khilaf)
If the first conditional divorce was restricted to three (e.g., 'أنت طالق ثلاثاً ما لم أطلقك'), and the second is unrestricted, only one divorce falls—the unconditional one. The husband retains two divorces. If both had fallen, he would have only one remaining. The text explains similar variations with two or three.
This illustrates the importance of the dispute: the number of remaining divorces affects whether the husband can revoke or reunite.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي أنت طالق ما لم أطلقك ، أنت طالق ، تطلق بالأخيرة
[١]
( وفي أنت طالق ما لم أطلقك ، أنت طالق ، تَطْلُقُ بالأخيرة) : أي إن قال : أنت طالق ما لم أطلقك ، أنت طالق ، تطلق بالأخيرة، وهي قوله : أنتِ طالق ؛
[۲]
حتى لو قال : أنتِ طالق ثلاثاً ما لم أُطلقك ، أنت طالق، تقع واحدة". [١]قوله : وفي أنت ... الخ ؛ يعني لو قال : أنت طالق بعد قوله : أنت طالق ما لم أطلقك أو متى لم أطلقك موصولاً من دون تخلّل السكوت يقع الطلاق منجزاً بالجملة الأخيرة لا بالتعليق. والقياس أن يقع المضاف إلى الزمان أيضاً، فيقعان جميعاً إن كانت مدخولاً بها، وبه قال زفره ؛ لأنه وجد زمان خال عن التطليق ، وإن كان قليلاً، وهو زمان قوله : أنت طالق قبل أن يفرغ منه.
ووجه الاستحسان : أنّ زمانَ البرّ مستثنى عن اليمين بدلالة الحال ؛ لأنّ البرهو المقصود، كما إذا حلف لا يسكن هذه الدار، واشتغل بالنقلة من ساعته تلك ، فإن قال : أنت طالق مفصولاً عن قوله : أنت طالق ما لم أطلقك وإن قل الفصل، وقعا اتفاقاً، قياساً واستحساناً ؛ لوجود الزمان الخالي عن التطليق. كذا في «النهاية» و«العناية»(۱).
[٢] قوله : حتى ... الخ ؛ بيان لثمرة وقوع المنجزة دون المعلقة، وهي أنه لو كان الطلاق الأوّل مقيداً بالثلاث أو الاثنين، وكان الثاني معـرى عـن العـدد تطلق واحدة فقط، وتظهر ثمرته عند كون الطلاق المعلّق واحداً أيضاً، وهي أنه يملك بعده طلقتين ، ولو كان المعلق والمنجز كلاهما واقعين لم تبق إلا واحدة.
[٣] قوله : تقع واحدة ؛ ولو كان الثاني مقيداً باثنتين يقع اثنان بالجملة الأخيرة، ويبقى له واحد، ولو كان مقيداً بالثلاث لا يظهرُ حينئذ ثمرة وقوع المنجز دون المعلق.
(۱) ((العناية (٤ : ٣٥ - ٣٦).
And in (the case of) "You are divorced unless I divorce you, (then) you are divorced", she becomes divorced by the last (utterance). [1] (The phrase "And in 'You are divorced unless I divorce you, you are divorced', she becomes divorced by the last") means: if he says: "You are divorced unless I divorce you, you are divorced", she becomes divorced by the last, which is his statement "You are divorced". [2] Even if he said: "You are divorced three times unless I divorce you, (then) you are divorced", one divorce occurs. [1] His statement: "And in 'You are divorced...' etc." means: if he says "You are divorced" after his statement "You are divorced unless I divorce you" or "whenever I do not divorce you" continuously without a pause, the divorce occurs as an immediate (munjiz) divorce by the last sentence, not by the suspended (mu'allaq) one. By qiyas, it should also occur with the one tied to time, so both would occur if she is a consummated wife, and this is the view of Zufar; because there is a time free of divorce, even if short, which is the time of his saying "You are divorced" before he finishes it. The basis of istihsan: the time of fulfilling (al-birr) is exempted from the oath by contextual evidence (dilalat al-hal); because fulfilling the oath is the intended purpose, just as if he swore not to live in this house and occupied himself with moving out from that very hour. If he says "You are divorced" separately from his statement "You are divorced unless I divorce you", even if the separation is short, both occur by agreement, by qiyas and istihsan, because there is a time free of divorce. Thus in al-Nihayah and al-Inayah (1). [2] His statement: "Even if... etc." is an explanation of the consequence of the occurrence of the immediate (munjiz) without the suspended (mu'allaq), namely that if the first divorce was restricted to three or two, and the second was free of number, she becomes divorced only once, and its consequence appears when the suspended divorce is also one, namely that he owns two divorces after it, and had both the suspended and immediate occurred, only one would remain. [3] His statement: "One divorce occurs": and if the second was restricted to two, two occur by the last sentence, and he has one left, and if restricted to three, then the consequence of the occurrence of the immediate without the suspended does not appear. (1) Al-Inayah (4:35-36).
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
The passage type is a ruling with proof (istihsan vs qiyas). The commentary (sharh) explains a ruling from the matn: if a husband says 'أنت طالق ما لم أطلقك' (you are divorced unless I divorce you) and then immediately says 'أنت طالق' (you are divorced) without a pause, the divorce takes effect by the second utterance, not the first suspended one. The first utterance is a conditional divorce that is suspended on a future event (not divorcing her), but the immediate utterance overrides it. The qiyas would suggest that both apply because there is a moment between them free of divorce (the time of uttering the second phrase before completion), but the Hanafi ruling based on istihsan is that only the second applies because the time of fulfilling the oath (birr) is exempt from the suspension by contextual evidence. Zufar disagreed. The author then discusses the consequence: if the first suspended divorce was for three or two, and the second is unrestricted, only one divorce falls (the immediate one), leaving the husband with remaining divorces. If the second is restricted to two, two fall, etc.

Key Terms
المعلقة (al-mu'allaqa): The divorce that is suspended on a condition (here: 'unless I divorce you').
المنجز (al-munajjaz): The immediate, unconditional divorce (here: the second 'أنت طالق' that is not suspended).
البر (al-birr): Fulfillment of an oath (here: fulfilling the condition by not divorcing).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of 'أنت طالق ما لم أطلقك، أنت طالق' without pause, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) Both the suspended and immediate divorces occur.
B) Only the first conditional divorce occurs.
C) Only the immediate unconditional divorce occurs.
D) No divorce occurs because the condition is impossible.

Key Takeaway
When a conditional divorce is immediately followed by an unconditional divorce without pause, only the unconditional divorce takes effect by istihsan, because the time of fulfilling the oath is exempted from the condition.
